Ministry of Finance's Proposal for Reorganizing Taxation Has Been Drafted; Fiscal Conference Opens on the 21st

(Nanjing) The National Fiscal Conference of this term is scheduled to open on the 21st. The Ministry of Finance is paying special attention to the abolition of miscellaneous taxes and the reorganization of land taxes. The draft proposal has been completed and submitted to the Secretariat of the Fiscal Conference for research. There are four proposals: 1. Reorganize the standards for business tax, advocating for defining the scope of collection to avoid double taxation. 2. Establish the minimum principle for land tax surcharges, advocating that any province or city collecting temporary land tax surcharges for more than three months must submit it to the central government for approval, and provincial governments cannot freely increase them. 3. Reorganize procedures for tax matters for the sake of unification. 4. The compensation plan after the cancellation of miscellaneous taxes. The principle has been determined, and detailed measures are being formulated by the Accounting Department in conjunction with the revenue and expenditure situations of various provinces and cities. The above four proposals will be submitted to the Secretariat of the General Assembly after Minister Kong's review. (11th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) It has been decided that Yang Dezhao, director of the Guangdong Provincial Government's Beijing office, will represent Guangdong Province at the financial conference, as Guangdong Provincial Finance Director Qu Fangpu is unable to come to Beijing to attend. (11th Special Dispatch)

(Changsha) Zhang Kailian is scheduled to go to Beijing on the 15th to participate in the fiscal conference. (11th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) He Shaoqiong is scheduled to enter Beijing on the 16th to attend the National Fiscal Conference. (11th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Lu Muting, Director of the Hebei Department of Finance, and Wang Zhicheng, Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau, are scheduled to depart for Beijing on the 17th to attend the National Fiscal Conference. (11th Special Dispatch)

Legislative Yuan Discusses Organizational Laws of Various Agencies; Some Advocate Abolishing the Anti-Opium Association

(Nanjing) On the 11th, the Legislative Yuan discussed revising the organizational laws of various agencies, specifically regarding the exercise of powers in the budget, accounting, and statistics sections. In the review report, it was stated that the Anti-Opium Association exists in name only and cannot exercise its functions. Therefore, there is no need to establish such an agency, and its organizational law need not be revised. Many members advocated suggesting that the central government abolish the association. Luo Yunyan advocated maintaining it and suggested that the central government convene a national anti-opium conference to discuss practical measures and actively combat opium use. It was later decided to discuss it separately. (11th Special Dispatch)

Jiangsu Provincial Government Approves Measures to Prohibit Opium Within a Time Limit

(Zhenjiang) The outline of the Jiangsu Province's measures to prohibit opium within a time limit was approved at the provincial government meeting on the 11th. The summary is as follows: (1) The main purpose of opium prohibition in this province is to completely eliminate it within a time limit, not to raise funds. (2) Anti-opium committees will be established at the provincial and county levels. (3) The time limit for complete opium prohibition in this province is four years. (4) During the period before prohibition, the supply of opium will be controlled by the government within a certain limit, allowing licensed operation. (5) Opium users in this province are required to apply for opium-smoking licenses from June 1st to August 31st of this year, which will be issued by the government, ordering them to quit in stages. After this period, no more licenses will be issued. (6) Unlicensed operation and unlicensed smoking after September 1st of this year will be treated as private trafficking and private smoking, and the Military Affairs Commission will be petitioned to handle them according to military law. (7) Those who request to quit smoking during the license period will be sent to the hospital for free detoxification. (8) Trafficking, manufacturing, and using morphine, heroin, and other narcotics will be petitioned to the Military Affairs Commission for severe punishment according to military law. (9) Fees and fines from anti-opium licenses will be used for anti-opium and construction purposes. (11th Special Dispatch)

Soil from the Yellow River Transported to Germany for Testing; Shen Yi Sent to Participate

(Nanjing) Mr. Tingges, a German expert, conducted experiments on the Yellow River regulation in the testing grounds in Germany. Due to a shortage of funds, he was unable to complete the experiment. It is said that the experiment requires an additional 60,000 yuan in national currency. The Yellow River Water Conservancy Association requested the Economic Council to allocate funds for subsidies, and 10,000 was remitted in full on the 10th. At the same time, Shen Yi was sent to Germany to participate in this experiment. The Yellow River Association specially packaged 2,000 kilograms of Yellow River soil, accompanied by soil sampling diagrams, and transported them to Germany for testing by Director Shen. (11th Special Dispatch)

Mountain Floods in Southern Hubei Continue to Rise

(Hankou) Mountain floods in southern Hubei continue to rise. Chongyang and Dasha Ping have become swamps. Chen Jicheng telegraphed the headquarters, saying that the water is about to cross the city walls. (11th Special Dispatch)

Citizens Continue to Be Poisoned in the Ximen Area of Beijing-Hankou; The Cause Has Not Yet Been Determined

(Nanjing) Seven more people were poisoned in Ximen, Hankou, on the 11th. They were immediately sent to the Health Bureau for treatment and recovered. However, the specific poison has not been identified despite testing. The bureau has sent it to Liang Qikui, a technician in the Chemistry Department of the Health Administration, for testing. At the same time, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau notified the police bureau that the sale of salt and vegetables in that area should be suspended until the case is clarified. (11th Special Dispatch)

Current Commentary

The Lytton Report is Published

— Ting

After the publication of the Lytton Report, Japanese officials recklessly criticized it. The real target of their opposition is not Lytton himself, nor the report itself, but the concrete facts and circumstances after the implementation of the report's recommendations. This can be easily understood without further explanation.

Although technical cooperation between the League of Nations and its member states is the responsibility of the League of Nations, and technical cooperation between China and the League of Nations is China's right. This is purely a matter between the League of Nations and its member states, and no third party is allowed to interfere. Moreover, technical cooperation between the League of Nations and its member states is not new and did not start with China. China's technical cooperation with the League of Nations began as early as the beginning of the 18th year of the Republic of China and did not start today. Japan does not oppose other countries cooperating with the League of Nations, and it only opposes it after expressing its withdrawal from the League of Nations while serving as a member of the Council of the League of Nations. Its insincere political interference is extremely obvious. We believe that the purpose of the Japanese move is, on the one hand, to passively threaten China to stop cooperating with the League of Nations, and, on the other hand, to actively stimulate and control China, forcing it to act hastily, and then using it as an excuse for further partitioning. Or it is to coerce China into dealing with them alone in order to realize their proclaimed Monroe Doctrine of East Asia. Therefore, even if we stop cooperating with the League of Nations due to unbearable pressure from the Japanese, it will still not be enough to slightly reduce their ambition to invade. It can be asserted that now that the Lytton Report has been published, the time for its implementation is even closer. Considering the situation, there is no reason to abandon it halfway. However, we do not have to lose heart because of the Japanese's one-sided opposition, nor can we not carefully consider the difficulties ahead. We believe that the key to whether future technical cooperation with the League of Nations can proceed without unexpected events lies in two points: (1) preventing the Japanese side from sabotaging it, and (2) avoiding the intrusion of political and economic forces of the great powers. These two points are closely related to the investment issue. Recently, the Japanese have opposed cooperation between the League of Nations and China, using the reorganization of old debts as a threat. Their focus is on the financial assistance from Europe and the United States. In the past, the content of technical cooperation between the League of Nations was limited to the hiring of experts and the connection of technical institutions between China and foreign countries, without involving investment. We should still fully understand this meaning and use the local capital as much as possible with the help of experts to create the environment and foundation for future economic construction. Even when foreign capital is needed, it should be utilized only after strictly stipulated conditions are met. For example, the regulation of the cotton and silk industries and the various proposals for water conservancy and road construction mentioned in the Lytton Report all contain serious international investment competition components. When implementing them, we should be very careful. We must know that technical cooperation is a relationship between the League of Nations and its member states, while investment for the implementation of cooperation plans is a relationship between creditors and debtors and should not be confused.

As for the foreign experts, we should only regard them as our consultants and advisors in their individual capacities, not as representatives of their countries. The tasks of each person have been clearly defined, limited to certain types or groups of work, and they should not be allowed to overstep their authority. If this can be done, it can reduce the excuses of the Japanese and the crisis of intrusion by the powers.

Japan Opposes Technical Cooperation; We Have No Response Yet

(Nanjing) According to outside information, after the Japanese side made an unofficial statement on April 17 regarding technical cooperation, it was severely refuted by the international community. The Japanese side also knew that it had caused resentment and then added evasions. After the publication of the Lytton Report, the Japanese propaganda became more intense, even saying that they were prepared to protest internationally. Our country is currently taking a wait-and-see attitude towards the Japanese side's attitude and has not expressed its position yet. If the Japanese side announces a formal document, it will be refuted again. (11th Special Dispatch)

Full Text of the Lytton Report by the League of Nations Technical Cooperation Representative

Preface

Since the International League of Nations has entered into a technical cooperation agreement with our country, it has appointed Dr. Rajchman, Director of the Health Section of the League of Nations, as its representative for technical cooperation in China. Mr. Rajchman came to China in October of the 22nd year. Recently, the Council of the League of Nations and the China Technical Cooperation Committee are scheduled to meet in Geneva on May 14th. Technical cooperation with our country will also be discussed. Therefore, he left China for Europe on April 10th to attend the meeting and report. Before leaving, he compiled an English report on his work in China for the League of Nations and sent a copy to our committee for reference. Now, we have translated and printed it according to the original report. The wording has not been changed. As for the sections related to our committee, please refer to our committee's other publications for more details.

Introduction

I. Upon examining the matter of China undertaking economic construction and technical cooperation with the League of Nations, the Chinese government previously sent a note to the League of Nations Council on June 28, 1933, stating therein:

My government previously sent a telegram to your League on April 25, 1931, stating in brief that my government had decided to establish a National Economic Council as an organ for planning national economic construction, and requesting cooperation with the technical organs of your League in carrying out such work. Your Council duly submitted this telegram for discussion at its meeting in May of the same year. In order to make the cooperation effective, my government also put forward several measures as follows:

(1) During the preliminary design and preparatory organization period, the League of Nations may, by analogy with the method of sending commissioners to China to assist in health affairs, send personnel to China to contribute their opinions on construction plans and how the League of Nations can assist in their implementation. The period of stay of such personnel in China shall depend on the actual needs and the convenience of the Chinese government.

(2) For the implementation of special projects, the League of Nations, at the request of the Chinese government, may dispatch or recommend officials, representatives, or specialists to China to assist. In addition to possessing their specialized skills, these personnel must be able to maintain constant contact with the relevant technical organs in Geneva.

(3) In special and appropriate circumstances, the League of Nations, at the request of the Chinese government, may designate existing committees or specially established committees to assist the Chinese government in formulating or improving special designs.

(4) For the sake of future expansion, there is a need to cultivate talent. The League of Nations can use appropriate methods to assist the Chinese government in training talent. For example, in the field of health, the League of Nations has been able to arrange for Chinese personnel to practice specialized work in other countries, sometimes with subsidies.

(5) In addition, the League of Nations can assist the Chinese government in identifying consultants to assist China in improving its education system and facilitate mutual communication between Chinese and foreign cultural centers.

The above-mentioned measures were approved by your Council at its meeting on May 19, 1931, and the methods for implementing the cooperation proposed by the Secretary-General of the League of Nations were also approved at the same time. The resolution on the first measure is as follows:

The officials dispatched to China in accordance with the first measure should be thoroughly familiar with the work of the League of Nations technical organs and be able to inform the Chinese government on how to utilize these organs. Furthermore, in accordance with the Secretary-General's opinion, one of the heads of the aforementioned technical organs should be stationed in China.

As for items two, three, and four proposed by my government, the resolution of your Council is as follows:

Regarding the various measures proposed by the Chinese government, the Secretary-General should notify the relevant technical organs to handle them and submit them to the Council for approval in accordance with the regulations.

More than two years have passed since your Council's resolution. During this period, my government has greatly benefited from the assistance of experts dispatched by the technical organs of your League of Nations and from the two senior officials of the Secretariat of your League of Nations who served as liaisons between my country and the various technical organs of your League of Nations. This person, during his several months of service in my country, performed his duties with remarkable success. Furthermore, the Secretary-General of your League of Nations has repeatedly recommended several technical personnel for my government to employ. For all of these, my government should express its deep gratitude to the Secretary-General of your League of Nations and your Council.

Now that my government has completed its preliminary investigation, it has decided to start economic construction work in several provinces, based on its financial capacity, as a starting point and as a model for the remaining regions of the country.

It goes without saying that the success of this economic construction work depends on the continued efforts of all those involved and the appropriate allocation of all undertakings. My government sincerely hopes that the methods adopted by your Council under the present circumstances will enable the continued cooperation between your League of Nations and my government on economic construction. In particular, it is hoped that a technical expert will be recommended and dispatched to my country as the technical cooperation representative of your League of Nations with my government and the National Economic Council.

If the above-mentioned matters can be submitted for discussion as soon as possible, so that all resolutions can be implemented at an early date, it would be greatly appreciated.

II. At its meeting on June 30, 1933, the Council of the League of Nations resolved to designate the Committee on Technical Cooperation between the League of Nations and China to review how the League of Nations should handle the above-mentioned note from the Chinese government. This committee then convened a meeting in Paris on July 18, 1933, and its resolution was approved by the Council of the League of Nations on the same day. The contents are as follows:

The Council of the League of Nations should, at the request of the Chinese government, appoint a representative for technical cooperation, whose mission is purely technical in nature and does not involve politics. In accordance with this principle, the representative for technical cooperation will be the technical liaison officer between the League of Nations and the National Economic Council, handling technical cooperation affairs between China and the relevant organs of the League of Nations.

The term of office of the representative for technical cooperation should be one year, and his salary, travel expenses, and living expenses will be provided by the Chinese government.

The duties of the representative for technical cooperation are as follows:

(1) To provide China with reports on the work of the various technical organs of the League of Nations and, in order to enable China's economic construction to cooperate internationally, to contribute to the Chinese government on how to utilize the various organs of the League of Nations.

(2) Upon receiving a request from the Chinese government for technical cooperation, the representative for technical cooperation should immediately forward it to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations for transmission to the relevant organs of the League of Nations.

(3) The representative for technical cooperation should assist the Chinese government if it wishes to continue to employ foreign technical experts for economic construction work.

(4) The representative for technical cooperation should assist the National Economic Council in properly allocating the duties of the technical experts stationed in China by the League of Nations on the ground. The representative for technical cooperation should report his work to the Council of the League of Nations from time to time, and at least once every three months, in detail. All technical organs of the League of Nations that have cooperated at the request of the Chinese government should also be informed by the Secretary-General of the League of Nations of this report. When performing the above-mentioned duties, if there are matters that require consultation with the various technical groups and technical organs in order to obtain their assistance, he should apply to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations.

Whenever the representative for technical cooperation submits a record of events or a work report to the League of Nations, he should also submit a copy to the National Economic Council.

The Committee on Technical Cooperation between the League of Nations and China appointed Dr. Rajchman, Director of the Health Section of the Secretariat, as the representative of the League of Nations for technical cooperation in China. His duties are as described above.

When informing the Council of the League of Nations of its resolution, the Committee on Technical Cooperation between the League of Nations and China stated that it would continue to listen to the instructions of the Council in order to (1) consider the issues of technical cooperation raised by the Chinese government to the Council of the League of Nations regarding economic construction undertakings, (2) review the reports and statements of the representative for technical cooperation, and discuss or review all issues concerning the performance of the representative's duties.

III. I obeyed the instructions of the Council of the League of Nations and took office in China on October 3, 1933, in accordance with the methods agreed upon with the Chinese government.

IV. On September 23, 1933, the National Government of China promulgated the revised organizational regulations of the National Economic Council, specially appointing President Wang Jingwei of the Executive Yuan, President Sun Ke of the Legislative Yuan, and Minister Song Ziwen of the Ministry of Finance as members of the National Economic Council, and all were designated as standing committee members. On October 4, Wang, Sun, and Song took office as standing committee members.

V. Later, Minister Song Ziwen resigned from the position of Minister of Finance, and the number of standing committee members of the National Economic Council was expanded from three to five. The National Government of China then additionally appointed the new Minister of Finance, Kong Xiangxi, and Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the Military Affairs Commission as standing committee members. Kong and Chiang took office as standing committee members on December 20 and 27, respectively.

VI. After the standing committee members took office one after another, they discussed in detail the various undertakings to be undertaken or subsidized in 1934, and also reviewed the various economic construction works that were already in progress.

VII. After the National Economic Council completed its preliminary research, it submitted the procedures for technical cooperation with the League of Nations to me for discussion. I sent this procedure to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations on December 30, 1933.

In my letter of December 30, 1933, to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, before explaining the main points of the National Economic Council's proposal, I suggested to the Secretary-General that the number of experts selected to go to China for service should be kept to a minimum. The selection of these experts should be based on those who have served in several countries and have rich experience in their work, or they should be prepared to stay in China for a longer period of time so that they can become familiar with local conditions. At the same time, I also stated that the cooperation between the League of Nations' health, transportation, and economic organs and the Chinese government has been extended to 1934, and that a political advisor sent to China is also continuing to conduct research.

The main undertakings planned by the National Economic Council for 1934 were the improvement of transportation, the regulation of water conservancy, and the implementation of large-scale rural construction in several regions.

The National Economic Council believes that highway construction has reached a considerable level and needs to be discussed with engineers who have served in countries with similar situations to China in order to improve it. The issues to be discussed are mainly the following four:

(1) What kind of road surface is most suitable for highways in designated areas?

(2) Methods of using highways.

(3) Locally available fuels.

(4) The most suitable types of vehicles and engines.

Therefore, the Transport and Communications Section of the League of Nations was requested to engage experts to go to China for consultation. As for water conservancy issues, an engineer with international experience was also requested to serve as an advisor to China on the implementation of water conservancy policies.

I suggested that the number of experts dispatched this time be limited to three to serve as advisors, and that each expert should be outstanding in talent and knowledge, and accompany the head of the Transport and Communications Section of the League of Nations to China.

The Ministry of Education has requested the League of Nations to send education experts to China to discuss how to implement the various recommendations made by the International Education Survey Group sent to China by the International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation two years ago, and by the Chinese Education Survey Group sent to Europe in 1932. The Ministry also hopes that the personnel selected by the League of Nations can serve as permanent liaison officers between China and the League of Nations' Committee on Intellectual Cooperation. The duties of the liaison officer should be:

(1) To prepare specialized research materials for educators going to Europe for study.

(2) To identify experts at the request of the Chinese government to serve as advisors to China on the reform of special education matters.

(3) To guide the studies of Chinese students studying abroad.

At that time, the Council of the League of Nations suggested that a person with experience and ability to coordinate educational policies with widespread industrial construction policies should be selected immediately.

The National Economic Council attaches great importance to Professor Terzaghi's agricultural survey in China and hopes that he will return as soon as possible. If Professor Terzaghi cannot accept the invitation to go to China, then the League of Nations is requested to recruit experts with experience in land reform in various agricultural countries in post-war Europe to select outstanding scholars to replace him. Those with experience in the work and methods of the economic committees of Europe, America, and the Soviet Union are particularly suitable for recruitment.

In addition, it was also inquired whether Professor Baileyga could work at the Geological Survey Institute in Beiping. Professor Baileyga was previously appointed by the League of Nations and served at the Central University in Nanjing for two years.

Since 1932, Dr. Mari has been appointed by the Economic Committee of the League of Nations as an expert in sericulture improvement in China at the request of the Chinese government. Since January 1, 1934, he has been employed as a commissioner of the National Economic Council. The Chinese government intends to request the League of Nations to recommend an expert with French sericulture experience to serve in the same position. Part of the salaries of these two sericulture experts will be borne by the League of Nations.

VIII. When the Committee on Technical Cooperation between the League of Nations and China of the Council of the League of Nations met on January 10, 1934, I requested the permission of the Council of the League of Nations to submit a detailed report at a later date because the implementation plan for technical cooperation was still under consideration. Therefore, on the 4th of the same month, I first submitted a short essay outlining the progress, stating:

The Chinese government leaders deeply agree with the motion of the Council of the League of Nations to promote technical cooperation between the League of Nations and China, and the various important groups in China also consider it satisfactory. The standing committee members of the National Economic Council are currently the President of the Executive Yuan, the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, the Minister of Finance, the President of the Legislative Yuan, and the important politician Song Ziwen. All agencies are happy to cooperate, and it is expected that the results will be good. The funds for the council's undertakings will be allocated from the US cotton and wheat loan, and it is hoped that a method can be determined soon. The new construction plan is being thoroughly studied. The original construction work on highways, water conservancy, rural construction, education, and public health is still continuing. The 1934 cooperation plan with the League of Nations for the above-mentioned work has been sent to the Secretary-General together with opinions for the technical groups to study. Please allow for a delay in submitting a detailed report. After Chinese and foreign experts have conducted economic surveys and reached conclusions, and the Chinese government has determined a specific plan, a detailed report will be submitted. In the future, reports on various tasks will continue to be submitted to the technical groups as usual, and progress will be reported to the Secretary-General on schedule for verification.

IX. The National Economic Council is currently continuing to carry out sanitation, road construction, and water conservancy projects. The newly determined work is also being investigated and researched in detail by Chinese and foreign staff and experts in accordance with procedures. Mr. Colson and Mr. Stampar are participating in this investigation and research work separately, as described below.

X. The National Economic Council's 1934 business plan was approved by the Standing Committee meeting of the council and then passed by the plenary session of the council on March 26 of this year.

XI. Regarding how to obtain the cooperation of the technical organs of the League of Nations in the various ongoing businesses and the various undertakings planned for 1934, I have exchanged letters many times with the Secretary of the Committee on Technical Cooperation between the League of Nations and China of the Council of the League of Nations, and have discussed them extensively. These letters are of great importance.

Chapter 1 History of the National Economic Council

I. In May 1931, the National Government of China decided to establish the National Economic Council. At that time, domestic turmoil was being quelled, and the provinces of Central China, North China, Southwest China, and Northeast China were following the orders of the central government. The world economic crisis had not yet affected China, so there were many hopes for peaceful development. The Chinese government eagerly hoped that technical cooperation between the League of Nations and China could be implemented as soon as possible. When the survey group sent to China by the International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation was still en route, and other technical personnel were also about to travel east, the Yangtze River basin (Note 1) suddenly suffered an unprecedented flood. Therefore, the League of Nations, at the request of the Chinese government, appointed the most experienced experts of the League of Nations to serve as the Deputy Chairman of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee (Note 2).

In the autumn of 1931, the economic crisis of the leading industrial countries of the West became more urgent. For example, the United Kingdom's abandonment of the gold standard was a clear indication.

On September 18 of the same year, the Japanese army occupied Shenyang. As a result, the emergency relief work in the Yangtze River basin that the Chinese government was handling and the central economic development agency that was being organized and waiting to be established were frustrated.

I. However, in the midst of these internal and external troubles, the National Economic Council was still able to hold its first plenary meeting on November 15 of the same year. Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the National Government and Chairman of the Council, delivered a speech at the opening of the meeting, detailing the purpose of establishing the Council, stating in brief:

(Note 1) Refer to the report of the National Government Flood Relief Committee.

Chapter 4

(Note 2) Sir John Hubert Marshall, Former Director-General of Archaeology in India

Looking at the organizational regulations of this council and the selection of committee members as announced on June 6th and September 26th of the 20th year of the Republic [1931], it can be seen that the purpose of the National Government in establishing this council was to set up an advisory body so that various parts of the government could closely liaise with all sectors of society, assisting the government in planning and implementing an urgent construction program. As for the government's selection of people from all walks of life as committee members, it was not due to their current political status, but because of their individual talents and reputation, their outstanding achievements in society, and their status as leaders in various fields. Therefore, from a general perspective, this council is indeed an advisory body, but sometimes, after the heads of various ministries accept the council's recommendations in their capacity as committee members, they can immediately put them into practice, so the council seems like an advisory body with executive functions.

Currently, various government agencies have many plans and suggestions regarding matters under their jurisdiction. The first important task of the council is to review and organize these plans, select the most essential and interrelated ones, prioritize them, and, within the shortest possible time, create a comprehensive plan that can be implemented within three years, starting from the 21st year of the Republic [1932]. From this, it can be seen that the council's responsibilities are very heavy. Article 3 of the council's organizational regulations clearly stipulates that all national economic construction or development plans, the economics of which are borne or subsidized by the national treasury, shall be reviewed and approved by the council before being submitted to the National Government for approval.

3. The work of the National Economic Council was originally expected to develop systematically at an early date, but due to the expansion of the Northeast Incident and the continuous flooding in the Central Plains, the government was forced to divert its attention and financial resources to those matters, and the council's development was thus thwarted. By early 1932, the national capital had moved west to Luoyang, far inland, and government work, except for the most urgent matters, had largely come to a standstill. All these extraordinary events, as well as the commercial decline and tax revenue reductions caused by the events, had already affected the national treasury's income, and the global economic recession, which China had previously avoided for various reasons, could no longer be escaped.

However, the National Economic Council, through painstaking efforts, continued to work on construction projects, such as continuing the unfinished work of the Flood Relief Committee, renovating the embankments of the Yellow River, the Yangtze River, and the Han River, the Gan River, and the Huai River, which were the most severely affected areas in central China, and assisting with water conservancy projects in Jiangbei, all of which were relatively significant.

As for road transportation, the National Economic Council has implemented two road construction plans. The first plan was implemented in the three provinces of Jiangsu, Anhui, and Zhejiang, which are located at the eastern end of the Yangtze River and are close to the central government. The second plan expanded the first plan to the four provinces of Hubei, Jiangxi, Hunan, and Henan. The funds required for road construction were allocated by the National Economic Council from the road construction fund, borrowing 40% of the required funds to be handed over to the respective provincial governments for construction. This approach is still ongoing, and the completed highways have reached 13,000 kilometers.

The National Economic Council took over existing health programs and, in accordance with the original three-year plan for developing health services, used them as tools for rural construction. It also established a central guidance and technical organization in Nanjing and organized rural experimental zones. The vast plans encompassed by both have been completed. Moreover, the Central Hospital and the Central Hygiene Experimental Institute have also been established, not only taking on the task of guiding medicine and public health, but also often engaging in organizing local health work at the request of provincial and municipal governments. The National Economic Council also investigated the general situation of agriculture and conducted detailed studies on the silk industry and social conditions in several provinces.

As for education, the National Economic Council also provided assistance to the Ministry of Education's research work at home and abroad.

4. During the first two years of the National Economic Council, the world economy continued to decline, and the southeastern and northern regions experienced warfare with the Japanese army. Southern and central China were often plagued by Communist bandits. Although the environment was difficult, work continued unabated. At the same time, cooperation with various technical organizations of the League of Nations also continued.

Dr. Boudreau, Director of the School of Hygiene in Warsaw, was appointed as the League of Nations Health Organization's representative in China from July 1930 and participated in all kinds of medical and health emergency work required by various disasters.

In October 1931, the League of Nations Educational Mission went to China. The members included Dr. Becker, former Minister of Education of Prussia; Professor Langevin of the Collège de France; Mr. Walski, former Director of Primary Education of the Polish Ministry of Education; and Professor Tawney of the University of London. This mission was sent by the International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation, accompanied by Mr. Henri Bonnet, the chairman of the committee, and Mr. Wald, the representative of the Secretary-General of the League of Nations. They studied the Chinese education system in China and submitted a report in July 1933, making suggestions for educational reform.

In early November 1931, Professor Choucroun and Dr. Huang Zifang, members of the Health Section of the League of Nations Secretariat, were sent to China to handle emergency prevention and medical work related to flood relief. Professor Choucroun served for three months, investigating infectious diseases in the Yangtze River basin, while Dr. Huang served for six months, mainly in charge of medical relief in Hankou. At the same time, Dr. Stampar, a member of the League of Nations Health Committee, participated in this epidemic prevention work for several months.

In early December, Mr. Bailey, a professor of geology at the University of Geneva, Dr. Weismann of the University of Vienna, and Mr. David, a lecturer in Chinese at the University of Nottingham, were invited by the Chinese Minister of Education and sponsored by the League of Nations to serve as lecturers at the National Central University in Nanjing for two years.

In January 1933, the League of Nations again sent Mr. Okinczyc, an advisor to the Polish Ministry of Public Works, as the representative of the League of Nations Transport and Transit Organization, and sent Mr. Potthoff, a water conservancy expert, to work with the National Economic Council, where they continue to work to this day.

In the same month, at the request of the Chinese government, the League of Nations Transport and Transit Organization commissioned Mr. Cotterell, a member of the Institution of Civil Engineers in London, Mr. Pinczon, the Inspector-General of Roads and Bridges in Paris, and Mr. Inveking, the director of the Port of Hamburg, to go to China to study the issues of diverting the Huai River and the port of Shanghai, as well as water conservancy in North China. Their recommendations are detailed in the National Economic Council's report on water conservancy projects.

In October of that year, Professor Dragoni, former Secretary-General of the International Institute of Agriculture in Rome, was recommended by the Economic Committee of the League of Nations and hired by the Chinese government to study the agricultural situation in China. His term was six months, and his report was submitted to the National Economic Council in 1933.

In the same month, Dr. Mari, president of the Italian Sericulture Association, was appointed by the Economic Committee of the League of Nations at the invitation of the Chinese government to study the Chinese silk industry, seeking ways to remedy it in order to revive the Chinese silk industry. From January 1934, he was hired as an official of the National Economic Council.

From March 1933, Mr. Shalon of the Economic and Financial Organization of the League of Nations stayed in China for six weeks at the invitation of the chairman of the National Economic Council to discuss the issue of the World Economic Conference and to coordinate the work of various experts of the League of Nations in China.

From May of the same year, Professor Molen, a professor at the Hamburg Institute for Tropical Diseases and a member of the League of Nations Malaria Commission, went to China to study the causes of malaria outbreaks and to suggest preventive measures to be adopted.

In the months that followed, Dr. Stanimir, former Director of Social Welfare and Public Health in Belgrade, was sent by the Health Organization of the League of Nations, and Mr. Clauson, Secretary of the Agricultural Association, was sent by the Economic and Financial Organization of the League of Nations, one after another. This was all due to the new plan for cooperation decided by the Council of the League of Nations on July 18 of that year.

Moreover, the Director of the Health Section and the Director of the Transport and Transit Section of the League of Nations Secretariat served as technical liaison officers from September 10 to December 16, 1931, and from January 1 to August 1931, respectively.

5. In the spring of 1933, the World Economic Conference convened in London. People around the world believed that the global economic and financial crisis could be resolved early through international consultation and measures. In April, the Chinese government, at the invitation of the U.S. President, specially sent Vice President Song Ziwen of the Executive Yuan (concurrently Minister of Finance and Vice Chairman of the National Economic Council) to the United States to consult with the U.S. government in advance, and led the Chinese delegation to attend the London Conference. In May of the same year, an agreement on cotton and wheat loans was reached with the U.S. Financial Reconstruction Corporation. Subsequently, consultations and discussions were held several times with various delegations attending the World Economic Conference and leaders of the industrial and commercial sectors of various countries on the prospects for cooperation in economic development. At this time, the Chinese government concluded a technical cooperation agreement with the Council of the League of Nations, the contents of which are detailed above.

6. The Chinese government established the National Economic Council as an organization for planning and implementing national economic construction. Therefore, the President of the Executive Yuan, the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, the President of the Legislative Yuan, the Minister of Finance, and former Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance Song Ziwen served as standing committee members. In addition, the ministers of various ministries such as Interior, Railways, Communications, Industry, and Education, as well as leaders from the intellectual and industrial circles and other sectors of society, were appointed as committee members so that all sectors could participate.

The functions of the National Economic Council are:

(1) Designing and reviewing national economic construction or development plans;

(2) Approving the funding required for national economic construction or development plans;

(3) Supervising and guiding national economic construction or development plans;

(4) Directly implementing specific economic construction or development plans.

The above items are extremely broad, defining the functions that the council should have, but not implying that they can be fully implemented at the current initial stage. As for the planning, supervision, and implementation of various projects, they are handled separately by various departments, specialized committees, and control committees and improvement committees.

The control committee or improvement committee is organized by representatives of the relevant departments whose work is related to the work of the committee, and another societal figure whose work is not related to the committee serves as its head. Once the plan of this committee is adopted by the National Economic Council, the committee is responsible for its implementation and, during implementation, can obtain political and economic support from the National Economic Council.

As for the organizational structure of the National Economic Council, specialized committees have been established for highways, water, health, education, and rural construction to discuss and plan. When the plans are implemented, specialized departments are established to preside over the work.

The departments that have been established now are: (1) the Secretariat, which, in addition to administrative staff, has eight technical experts and six foreign experts to handle technical matters, (2) the Highway Department, (3) the Health Experimental Department, (4) the Water Conservancy Department, and (5) the Agriculture Department.

In order to carry out its economic construction work, the National Economic Council needs to conduct economic surveys. However, in order to avoid duplication of work with existing agencies, it does not establish a special agency but assigns it to the Review Committee. The Director-General of the Academia Sinica serves as the chairman of the committee, and the Secretary-General of the council, the Director of the Geological Survey, and others serve as committee members. All technical plans and work of the National Economic Council are submitted to this committee for review. All economic survey matters that need to be handled are also assigned by this committee to various agencies or designated experts for handling.

The National Economic Council has decided to proceed cautiously with the establishment of committees responsible for implementation. Only the Cotton Industry Control Committee and the Silk Improvement Committee have been established so far.

7. The operating expenses of the National Economic Council, from 1931 to September 1933, totaled 4.55 million yuan, all of which was provided by the government.

8. The work completed by the National Economic Council during the preparatory period and the projects to be carried out from 1934 will be described in detail in the following chapters.

A Glimpse of Opinions in Various Countries After the Publication of the Rajchman Report

(London) After the publication of the work report by Dr. Rajchman, the League of Nations' technical cooperation representative, it has aroused keen attention from British public opinion. The Times has opened a special column to publish a summary of the report and added comments in the first editorial. In general, it clearly expresses sympathy for the efforts of League of Nations expert Rajchman. It stated, "Since Rajchman was commissioned as the representative for technical cooperation with China, he has always followed the principle of adhering to political neutrality when performing his duties as stipulated by the Committee on Technical Cooperation with China of the Council of the League of Nations. There is nothing to prove that he has overstepped political neutrality. Moreover, Japan also agreed to the principle of technical cooperation with China in Geneva. If Japan had not withdrawn from the League of Nations, it could have even served as a member of the Committee on Technical Cooperation. As for China, as a major republic in the Far East, the power to decide which method is most appropriate for China to seek foreign aid rests with China itself. So far, China has not requested loans from the League of Nations, and if China's railway administrative credit has not been fully established, and there is no real assurance that the loans will be used for their originally agreed purposes, it is not appropriate for foreign countries to lend money to China. In short, as China's internal organization becomes stronger, the whole world should look at it with new eyes, and it is in the common interest of the whole world for China to become more prosperous. This is undoubtedly true." On the other hand, the Labor Party's newspaper, "Daily Herald", commented on Rajchman's report by focusing on political issues, criticizing Japan's opinions on Rajchman's report, and launching another attack on Japanese imperialism. It also sarcastically advised the League of Nations to protect its prestige. The newspaper continued to say that Germany and Japan are increasingly friendly, as evidenced by the recent visit of Vice Admiral Matsushita to Germany. It must be known that the old German dynasty defied the world's moral consciousness, leading to its downfall, which can serve as a lesson for Japanese militarists. However, the League of Nations should not merely engage in empty threats and should take resolute action. If Geneva strengthens its defenses, even the most stubborn Japanese rulers will not dare to underestimate it. (Havas Agency, 11th)

(London) The Manchester Guardian commented on the Rajchman report today, saying that there is no issue of providing assistance to the Chinese army or financial assistance in this report. However, Japan loves its neighbor too much and does not allow it to receive the League of Nations' development, and it has seriously doubted Rajchman's plan to provide China with a few experts to help it help itself. Japan also suspects that there is a conspiracy to provide China with money, so it issued a semi-official and unfounded warning, urging the West not to interfere in China. However, Japan certainly has not forgotten that the member states of the League of Nations have a solemn obligation to assist China according to the outline proposed by Rajchman. (Reuters, 11th)

(Tokyo) Today, the Tokyo Asahi Shimbun published an editorial entitled "The League of Nations and Aid to China," the gist of which is as follows: Dr. Rajchman's report on the League of Nations' technical assistance committee to China claims that there is no political intention. However, does the report not contain any political effects that deviate from the relationship between China and Japan? We cannot help but have some doubts. Originally, why did the League of Nations specially select Dr. Rajchman, an extremely anti-Japanese figure with a well-established reputation, to go to China? This is really difficult for us to understand. Therefore, the League of Nations has had a sense of misjudgment in selecting people from the beginning. No matter how the League of Nations declares that its aid to China is only for the purpose of technical assistance, how can one expect a fair result from such a person? Now, it is only after listening to Dr. Rajchman's theory of limiting technical assistance to China that it has a value for consideration. (Dentsu, 11th)

Amid the Military Reduction Stalemate, France and China Vigorously Implement Naval Policies: In View of Germany's Reorganization of its Navy, Shipbuilding Programs are Included in the Budget

(Paris) The construction of the super-class cruiser "Dunkerque" may be included in the 1934 French naval budget. The ship has a displacement of approximately 23,000 tons. In addition, one or two cruisers similar to the "Dunkerque" may be built to complete the combat power of this type of warship. France's decision to build this new type of heavy ship is entirely due to Germany's construction of 10,000-ton cruisers. Although German ships do not violate the Treaty of Versailles, their power is beyond the reach of ordinary cruisers. Today, France's shipbuilding plan is more urgent than it was two years ago. Several of France's old ships will soon reach the end of their service life, and it is planned to replace them with new Magador-class destroyers. One of the new destroyers has already been included in the 1934 plan. The two submarines proposed for 1934, one for reconnaissance use, with a displacement of 1,500 tons, and the other for coastal patrol use, with a displacement of 600 tons, may replace the old ships. The naval budget for 1934 states that France has built too many submarines in the past few years, but there are still various reasons to continue the submarine policy and improve the mechanical shortcomings of submarines. The naval budget for 1934 is approximately 913,000,000 francs, which is lower than the budget for 1933. This is because the tonnage for 1934 is more limited, and building surface warships is less expensive than building submarines. The 913,000,000 francs in the budget include the funding for 1934 to 1939, of which 20 million francs will be used to continue the 1934 shipbuilding program. Its stipulated uses are as follows: 5 million francs will be used to build new ships, and the remaining 15 million francs will be used for naval artillery, coastal defense fleets, and armaments. (National Telegram, 11th)

German Envoy Meets with British Authorities to Secretly Discuss Military Reduction

(London) German military reduction envoy Ribbentrop told reporters today that his visit to London was informal, so he avoided making any remarks. Today, Mr. Ribbentrop visited Foreign Minister Simon and Lord Privy Seal Eden for a secret talk lasting about one and a half hours. Later, Mr. Ribbentrop announced that he had no other scheduled talks with British cabinet members. (Reuters, 10th)

(London) It is generally speculated that the short duration of the talks between Ribbentrop and Simon Eden was probably due to the fact that the views and proposals put forward by Ribbentrop were not approved by the British side. The motive for Ribbentrop's visit was ostensibly to discuss the possibility of the military reduction conference producing results. However, according to some sources, Ribbentrop criticized France's military buildup policy at the beginning of the talks, saying that Germany was committed to peace, unlike France. At that time, Simon and Eden immediately said that they found it difficult to agree with this view, and the United Kingdom could not adopt this position, meaning that Germany's policy of rebuilding its military cannot be said to be committed to peace, and the criticism of France is also unfair. Therefore, the opinions of the two sides differed greatly on this issue, and it was impossible to continue the discussion. However, it is generally believed that the talks also touched on the issue of limiting or abolishing aerial weapons, because only on this issue were the opinions not too conflicting, and there was a possibility of reaching an understanding. In short, since Ribbentrop's visit has failed, the only thing that Geneva can do its best in the future is whether it can conclude a convention restricting the use of aerial weapons. It is also only on this issue that there is still hope of success. (Havas Agency, 10th)

Henderson's Consultations in Paris Yield No Results

(Paris) Military reduction conference Chairman Henderson's meeting with Foreign Minister Barthou yesterday has generally been regarded by public opinion here as having not yet produced concrete results. According to the Morning Post, Henderson intended to propose to the French government a compromise solution for reducing aerial armaments, but in reality, whether or not this agreement can be reached depends on today's negotiations. In short, Henderson will return to London tonight. He does not want to return empty-handed, so he deeply hopes that this proposal can be successful, so that something is better than nothing. (Havas Agency, 11th)

(Paris) Today, military reduction conference Chairman Henderson and Foreign Minister Barthou consulted until 4 p.m. According to the news released by the press, Henderson and Barthou exchanged opinions for the first time today, which was very sincere. The talks between the two sides will continue tomorrow morning. It is reported that today's talks involved the situation of the Geneva military reduction conference. The French Council of Ministers this morning fully approved the position taken by Barthou.

This position is reflected in the note sent by France to the British government on April 17, which states that France cannot accept Germany's open rearmament, disregarding treaty obligations, and making it a legitimate act. The British cabinet is now considering solutions to this attitude of France, which Henderson must have expressed to Barthou today. In addition, London believes that if a general military reduction convention cannot be concluded, it may be possible to conclude a convention restricting aerial armaments. Henderson clearly pointed out this plan this morning. After detailed research on various facts, it can be seen that France may not change its wait-and-see attitude adopted since April 17. France may not have other suggestions besides the views expressed in the note of April 17. Moreover, the general public does not have much hope for the UK's initiative to conclude a convention restricting aerial armaments. Under these circumstances, whether it is appropriate to convene a meeting of the General Commission on Military Reduction on May 25 is a question that Henderson must resolve. However, the power to decide this issue is in Henderson's hands and will not be affected by the current talks. As for the French side, it has stated that it has always advocated holding a meeting on May 25. Even if this meeting does not achieve anything, at least the situation caused by Germany's rearmament can be made clear during the debate. (Havas Agency, 10th)

A Belgian Authority on International Law Sympathizes with Germany's Military Demands: France is in Danger if it Does Not Change its Attitude; The League of Nations Cannot Be Relied Upon as a Weapon

Brussels. Beulé, a well-known Belgian political scientist and authority on international law, published a valuable and frank paper in a prominent publication in Beijing today. According to Beulé's opinion, the Allied countries of the past now have a clear need to agree to Germany's military demands and continue negotiations with them. A former Belgian prime minister also said that today's Germany is different from the past, because today's Hitler can represent the people of the whole country and speak for them without fear of the people's disapproval. This is something that Stresemann or Brüning could not do in the past, and Brüning was never able to agree with public opinion. The reason why Hitler acts unilaterally is that he assumes full responsibility for his actions. At the end of his article, Beulé issued a warning to France, saying that in his personal opinion, France is on a dangerous path, because France's anti-German stance on the military reduction issue is an isolated action, and Geneva, which he relies on as a weapon, is unreliable. (National Telegram, 10th)

US Drought: Western Drought Unprecedented in Forty Years, Crop Losses Fifty Percent

Saskatchewan, United States: American agriculture is currently experiencing the most severe drought since 1894, compounded by hurricanes, dust storms, and pest infestations, leading to the devastation of farmlands in the Midwest. Daily losses of wheat and other agricultural products exceed one million bags. According to Secretary of Agriculture Wallace, this drought is unprecedented in the United States in forty years. The Associated Press's inspection today revealed that the agricultural disaster in various US states is exceptionally severe. The inspection area included the Great Lakes region in the north, extending to Mexico and Baja California in the south, and reaching the Rocky Mountains in the west, all marked by desolation and dust storms. Adding to the calamity is pest infestation. Although it rained last night, the scant rainfall provided little relief. The wheat harvest has been halved, totaling less than 500 million bags. If substantial rainfall does not arrive promptly, the newly planted wheat will face complete failure. Hurricane damage has been particularly severe, as strong winds have blown away topsoil, causing root systems to wither from soil loss. The Associated Press received reports from 352 villages across eleven federal states, all acknowledging significant crop damage, but assuring that sufficient wheat reserves exist to meet national needs. The Secretary of Agriculture stated that if the American Midwest does not receive ample rainfall, the total US wheat harvest would not exceed 450,000,000 bags, a shortfall of 200,000 bags compared to average years. However, previous wheat surpluses are sufficient to meet national demand. According to the Department of Agriculture's report, spring grain harvests were excellent. Statistics indicate that wheat production in 1934 should reach 461,047,000 bags, compared to 35,103,000 bags last year. The five-year average from 1927 to 1931 was 632,061,000 bags. The Department of Agriculture also stated that the combined drought and pest damage in the Mississippi and Missouri River basins is destroying approximately one million bags of wheat per day. (10th National Dispatch)

US Treasury: Deep Rift with Silver Faction, Government Concessions Too Far Apart from Silver Faction's Proposals, Silver Faction's Repeated Struggles Waning

(Washington) Silver faction senators today generally acknowledged that their proposals and the government's concessions were too far apart. This point was confirmed after an internal meeting of the Senate Silver Faction. Although Treasury Secretary Morgenthau is scheduled to continue meetings with Silver Faction senators tomorrow, Senator Thomas claimed this afternoon that the Treasury Department intends to obstruct any silver-related legislation. Thus, the widening rift between the Treasury Department and the Senate Silver Faction is evident. Thomas declared that even if Congress passes silver legislation, the Treasury Department would impede its implementation; therefore, to get the government to accept a specific silver purchase plan, national public opinion must be aroused. Thomas also predicted that the failure of the silver bill would lead to unfavorable economic developments. The rupture between the Treasury Department and the Silver Faction began at yesterday's meeting when Senator Borah expressed dissatisfaction and left the session upon hearing the second clause of the Treasury Department's draft. With the rift now deep, President Roosevelt must make a further decision on which silver bill he is prepared to accept. According to Senator Borah, Secretary of the Treasury Morgenthau's proposal is purely permissive, while the President had previously stated that any bill must be mandatory. It is now understood that both the Treasury Department and Silver Faction senators will appeal to the President, requesting his true intentions. According to a statement from the Senate today, government-aligned senators are prepared to pass any compromise bill. (10th National Dispatch)

(Washington) President Roosevelt has informed Treasury Secretary Morgenthau of the points on which he can accommodate the silver faction's views, so legislation clarifying the status of silver is expected to be introduced soon. Morgenthau reported to President Roosevelt on the results of his consultations with congressional silver faction senators and notified the Senate silver faction senators that the Treasury Department is prepared to continue discussions at any time. Some advocate abandoning the proposal to nationalize silver, but those involved believe this is inconsequential. (10th Reuters)

(Washington) Silver faction Senator King stated today that he remains optimistic about the prospects for silver legislation. According to his remarks to the press, "The United States will maintain a policy of gold and silver as currency; this is the gist of this silver bill." (10th National Dispatch)

(New York) The New York Commercial Bulletin's Washington dispatch reports that after prolonged negotiations between silver faction senators and the authorities, it is now rumored that the most the silver faction can expect is a very flexible bill that allows silver to be part of the US legal tender reserve. Congressional leaders have stated to President Roosevelt that, as far as the silver issue is concerned, what the White House says is law. (11th Reuters)

US State Department: Note to War Debt Nations, Prepared to Begin Negotiations

(Washington) Today, the State Department sent a note to the foreign diplomatic representatives of the war debt nations, stating that debtor nations making credit payments will still be considered delinquent under the provisions of the Johnson Act. State Department officials, adhering to President Roosevelt's policy, informed the foreign diplomatic representatives of the debtor nations that the United States is prepared to listen to any suggestions for reducing or settling war debts. Most war debts are due on June 15, but to date, no country has formally expressed its opinion on the matter. US Attorney General Cummings recently interpreted the provisions of the Johnson Act, stating that countries making credit payments on time should not be considered delinquent, because when the United States accepted these payments, it explicitly stated that it would no longer consider these countries delinquent. If the United States issues a formal notification in advance, it can claim that credit payments are insufficient to cover maturing debts and still invoke the provisions of the Johnson Act to bind debtor nations. The five countries that have previously made credit payments are Great Britain, Italy, Czechoslovakia, Latvia, and Lithuania. (10th National Dispatch)

(Washington) The State Department stated today that the act of debtor nations repaying a portion of their war debts to demonstrate creditworthiness still constitutes a default and is subject to the Johnson Act, which prohibits lending. However, credit payments may still be accepted to avoid complete cessation of payments. The US government's views on war debts will be further detailed in President Roosevelt's message to Congress. An early resumption of war debt talks between Great Britain and the United States could break the deadlock. State Department officials anticipate that British Ambassador to the United States Lindsay will soon visit the State Department to discuss the matter. A few days ago, Attorney General Cummings stated that Great Britain, Italy, Czechoslovakia, Latvia, and Lithuania are not considered in default under the Johnson Act because they have paid a portion of their debt to the United States as a sign of creditworthiness. This statement has been met with mixed reactions in Congress, with some deeming it invalid and others supporting it. Diplomatic circles believe that the Justice Department's ruling is very beneficial to Great Britain because it could reopen war debt negotiations. It was later heard that President Roosevelt would state in his message to Congress that he would no longer accept credit payments. However, today, the State Department said that credit payments may still be accepted. In short, the US government's attitude will be seen in the President's message to Congress. According to Reuters, British newspapers criticized President Roosevelt's views on war debts, saying that European debtor nations do not see any possibility of repaying the United States several million dollars in war debts. The Daily Express even stated in today's editorial that President Roosevelt should know that Britain will no longer repay war debts. (10th Reuters)

(Paris) The Council of Ministers discussed the French war debt to the United States this morning. The discussion was initiated by Foreign Minister Barthou, who submitted a report by French Ambassador to the United States de Laboulaye regarding the scope of the Johnson Act and the interpretation of US Attorney General Cummings for cabinet study. Barthou is scheduled to go to Geneva on Sunday to attend the League of Nations Council meeting. The war debt issue will be thoroughly studied again after Barthou returns from Geneva, when the Council of Ministers will hold another meeting. Furthermore, the Saar region plebiscite issue is one of the agenda items for the current session of the League of Nations Council. Barthou today specifically explained the French delegation's position. It is reported that Barthou will request various safeguards in Geneva from the League of Nations Council to hold the plebiscite in accordance with the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles. (10th Havas)

US Actively Planning Transatlantic Air Route

(Washington) The United States is currently preparing a transatlantic air route plan, with a scale no less than the long-distance air route traversing South America. Fearing that aviators from France, Germany, Britain, and other countries will preempt them, they are sparing no effort to promote this plan. American aircraft magnates are negotiating routes with foreign countries while accelerating the construction of powerful seaplanes domestically. Explorers and climate experts are busy surveying in the rarely visited regions of Greenland. Another air route is planned via Bermuda to Southern Europe and is also under negotiation and surveying. As for American aviation power, it has extended to 33 countries. Six large transatlantic seaplanes have been completed and are beginning practice flights in preparation for the transatlantic air route linking Europe and the Americas to operate on a regular schedule once opened. These seaplanes can carry 32 passengers and 1,000 pounds of mail. (10th National Dispatch)

Hejaz-Yemen War News: Troops Besiege City, Yemen Suing for Peace, France Sends Warships to the Red Sea

Cairo: News arriving here today states that Ibn Saud is expanding his Arabian territories and is progressing smoothly. Armed vehicles and cavalry have left the ancient Red Sea port of Hodeida to join the army attacking Sanaa, the capital of Yemen. Before reaching Sanaa, the army must pass through the difficult Khukha Pass, so they are proceeding cautiously to avoid ambushes. Also, according to news from Jerusalem, several former Turkish army officers have decided to join Ibn Saud's army. (Daily Reuters)

Russia Loses a Revolutionary Veteran: Chief of Secret Police Dies

(Moscow) The Central Committee of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union issued a notice stating that Vyacheslav Menzhinsky, head of the secret police (OGPU), has passed away. Menzhinsky was one of the most prominent representatives of the old Bolshevik guard, an uncompromising revolutionary fighter, a great organizer, and a leader in the struggle against counter-revolutionary forces. He was born on September 1, 1874, the son of a teacher, and received legal education. He joined the revolutionary movement at a young age and was an active member of the Bolshevik organization. After the 1905 revolution, he fled abroad. After the February Revolution in 1917, he returned to Russia and actively participated in the revolutionary movement again, preparing for the October Revolution. After the October Revolution, Menzhinsky served as Chairman of the Finance Committee in the first Soviet government. In 1918, he was appointed Consul General in Berlin. After returning from Germany, he served in the People's Commissariat for Foreign Affairs. After 1919, he served in the "Cheka" (All-Russian Extraordinary Commission for Combating Counter-Revolution and Sabotage), and after Dzerzhinsky's death in 1926, he succeeded him as the Minister of the State Political Directorate. (10th TASS)

Japanese Massacre Occurs in Brazil

(New York) The New York Times correspondent in the Brazilian capital reports that a Brazilian man fell in love with a Japanese woman, and was subsequently shot and killed by the woman's father. This sparked public outrage among local Brazilian farmers, who attacked the Japanese settlement, dragging the Japanese people out of their homes and beating them. A total of five Japanese people were beaten to death and sixteen were injured. (11th Reuters)

Japan and Uruguay Establish Reciprocal Trade Agreement: Adopting Market Diversification, Japanese Goods Flood In Without Limits

The capital of Uruguay: Trade negotiations between Japan and Uruguay have recently concluded. The new trade agreement has been signed by the Uruguayan government and the Japanese envoy, stipulating that the two countries' trade will be subject to most-favored-nation treatment. (10th Havas)

(Tokyo) As countries around the world try to prevent the inflow of Japanese goods, Japan is adopting a market diversification strategy to cope with countermeasures, striving to open up new markets while maintaining old ones. According to a certain survey, exports in Showa 8 (1933) increased significantly compared to Showa 7 (1932), with exports to Europe, Asia, and the Americas increasing by 18%. Exports to new markets such as Central America, South America, and Africa increased by 76%. Thus, new markets have become important for Japanese trade. (11th Japan United Press)

Russo-Japanese Fisheries Negotiations: Ruble Exchange Rate Issue Resolved

(Tokyo) It is now believed that the issues between Russia and Japan regarding fishing grounds and the ruble exchange rate have been effectively resolved. This is the result of today's discussions between the Japanese Foreign Minister and the Soviet Russian Ambassador to Japan. Soviet Russia has accepted Japan's proposal to begin negotiations on the ruble exchange rate and no longer insists on raising the exchange rate. It has also agreed to soon re-auction 47 fishing grounds. It is heard that Soviet Russia does not want to compete for 42 of them. The auction dispute arose on February 20 of this year, when Japanese people bid for certain fishing grounds in Vladivostok. Subsequently, they received a notice from the authorities stating that their bids, based on an exchange rate of 2.5 sen of Japanese gold per ruble, should be considered invalid because the exchange rate set by the Soviet Russian government was 7.5 jiao. Japan pointed out that Soviet Russia's auction unilaterally violated the provisional agreement signed in April 1931 by Kijūrō Shidehara and Troyanovsky and protested to Moscow. (11th Reuters)

Japanese Military Conducts Air Defense Exercises in Sinuiju and Antung: In Case of War with Soviet Russia, Yalu River Bridge May Be Bombed

Seoul: The Japanese 20th Division stationed in Korea will hold large-scale air defense exercises in Sinuiju and Antung on May 20. Participants include student groups, youth groups, local armies, officers and soldiers from the 20th Division and garrison troops, the Antung Japanese police garrison, and Japanese and puppet troops, all under the leadership of the Pyeonganbuk-do National Defense Association. Kwantung Army Commander General Hishikari and Korean Army Commander General Kawashima, along with other military and political figures, will be present to supervise and encourage. The objectives of the exercises are as follows: (1) How to prevent Russian air force bombing of the Yalu River railway bridge after the outbreak of war with Russia. (2) How to prevent Chinese and Korean people from blowing up bridges and disrupting transportation in the rear. (11th China United Press)

Fushun Coal Mine Explosion: Coal Car Falls, Killing and Injuring Over Twenty

Fushun: At 5:30 PM yesterday, in the Xintun mine of the Fushun Coal Mine, a methane gas explosion occurred in a coal car carrying Manchus as it entered the mine. The coal car fell on top of miners working below, killing fourteen people and seriously injuring eleven. The seriously injured were immediately sent to the South Manchuria Railway Hospital for treatment. The cause of the explosion is also under investigation. The coal mine is the newest one being mined, with thousands of technicians and miners, resulting in temporary chaos. (11th Denstu)

Zhai Zonghan, secretary of the Executive Yuan, received them and promised to forward the matter to President Wang for handling. Liang Hancao of the Legislative Yuan was seen. Zhao Guangting, section chief of the Ministry of Industry, received them. The Ministry of Industry will consult with the Ministry of Finance to cancel this illegal taxation.
