International Commercial Telegrams

Special Business Telegram from Reuters, May 10th

Gold and Silver: London Gold Price: Today's London gold price is higher again, at 136 shillings and one penny. Yesterday it rose one penny.

London Silver: In today's silver market, China and continental Europe sold, while the United States and speculators bought. The market closed steady, with the spot price at 19 pence 25 and the futures price at 19 pence 375, both up zero six. Five. The New York silver market loosened because of disappointing news from overseas and discouraging statements from leaders of the domestic silver faction. According to the leaders of the silver faction, the negotiation results they can obtain are nothing more than a flexible bill that makes silver part of the United States' legal reserve. However, the recent large-scale purchase of silver is the supporting factor in today's silver market. After the opening, there was some buying, and prices quickly became firm. There were not many transactions, as merchants wanted to wait for developments in Washington.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was extremely sluggish this morning, with no excitement. The opening price for British-American exchange was 5 dollars, 1 dime, 1 cent, and 375 mils, up 25 from yesterday's British-American closing price. The price rose slightly before noon. The latest price is 5 dollars, 1 dime, 1 cent, and 5625 mils, up 18715 from the opening price. Also, one US dollar is equivalent to 3 shillings and 10.927 pence in British gold.

British-French: The opening price was 77 francs 25, the same as yesterday's closing price. Before noon, there was no change. Later, it rose 9 pounds, to 77 francs 34.

British-American: Today's opening price was 5 dollars, 1 dime, 1 cent, and 625 mils, up half a point from yesterday's closing price. Later, it gradually fell 375 mils. The latest price is 5 dollars, 1 dime, 1 cent, and 25 mils.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The cotton market opened this morning with a bearish sentiment. It was initially stable, as purchases from Liverpool and continental Europe absorbed sales from local cash merchants in New Orleans and the South. Subsequently, due to favorable weather and weak spot demand, the cotton market was poor, and many parties engaged in liquidating positions, causing the market to trend downward. The Cotton Exchange estimates April consumption at 500,000 bales.

British Cotton: After falling yesterday, the Liverpool cotton market turned firm today. At 1:00 PM, the July futures price was 5.91, up six pounds.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market for July futures rose one penny and 125 mils, to 4 shillings, one penny, and 125 mils.

Rubber

London Market: The market was stable this morning. At noon, the trading price for July and September futures was 6 pence 625, up 125 mils from yesterday.

New York: The rubber market opened firmer today due to buying from traders and speculators. Sentiment was optimistic, but after recent activity, the market showed a tendency to be sluggish. There were not many transactions. After the price increased, the market stabilized.

Securities

New York Stock Market: Yesterday's rebound after the opening was not sustained. Today, there was a lot of selling at the opening. The market was mixed. Current prices have penetrated the low levels of March. This especially stimulated bearish sentiment in the market. Trading volume in the first hour after the opening this morning was 250,000 shares. Resolutions of the Jiangsu Provincial Government Meeting

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee held its 657th meeting on the 11th. The attending committee members were Chen Guofu, Cheng Tianfang, Yu Jingtang, Zhao Dihua, Shen Baixian, Zhou Fo Hai, and Wang Xiling. Chairman Chen Guofu resolved the following important cases: (1) The resignation of Li Guohua, the head of the Nanhui County Public Security Bureau, was approved, and Chen XiongTu was appointed to fill the vacancy. (2) The "Rules for Controlling Gifts for Weddings, Funerals, and Celebrations in the Province" were approved. (3) The rioters from Yangzhong County and the bandits from other counties were approved to be transferred to the relevant courts and the original counties for handling separately. (4) The "Organizational Regulations for the Public Funds and Property Management Offices in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province" were approved. (5) The "Provisional Regulations for the Examination and Certification of Primary School Teachers by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education" and the "Organizational Regulations for the Committee for the Examination and Certification of Primary School Teachers by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education" were approved. (6) The standing committee member and chairman of the Provincial Relief Committee, Gu Renfa, had resigned. Yu Jingtang was recommended to replace him as standing committee member and appointed as chairman. (7) The "Regulations for the Jiangsu Provincial County Government Assistant Personnel Training Institute" were approved. (8) The local budgets for the 22nd year of the Republic for six counties, including Changshu, Yizheng, Nantong, Jiangdu, Wujiang, and Wuxian, were approved. (9) The original method for assessing the collection of field taxes in the province will expire at the end of June. Due to the current economic distress in rural areas, a two-month extension is approved, and the counties are ordered to continue to urge collection until the end of August and report the results. The Provincial Department of Finance will incorporate the collections before the end of June for assessment. (10) Due to the strain on provincial funds, the subsidy for the Wuxian County Public Security Bureau will be reduced by 60,000 yuan from the 23rd year of the Republic, with an actual allocation of 139,850 yuan. American Industrial Recovery and Diplomacy New York Correspondence: Political Trends Shift with the Economy; Diplomacy is Powerless to Help Other Countries

American political action as a whole is focused on the Blue Eagle movement and the so-called "New Deal" policy. The actual content is about the same as before. In order to revive its domestic market, the US government spends 39 million US dollars every day, of which 19 million is lost and unrecoverable. Therefore, some people mock President Roosevelt, saying that he is a drunken sailor who only wants to spend money and has no other function. In fact, this kind of comment is also superficial and only recognizes one side of the actual situation in the United States. This side is the imbalance between agricultural and industrial development. Industrial manufactured products have increased due to the reduction in currency value and the stimulation of recovery, but agricultural products such as wheat have risen very little. However, looking at the entire US economic situation, there has been some progress, especially in the industrial sector. Now, according to a survey by the New York Times, based on the business activity index, assuming that its normal state is equal to 100, the amount of freight transportation on January 6 this year was 66.0, on February 10 it was 65.1, and on March 17 it was 69.4. Steel manufacturing in January this year was 53.0, in February it was 52.9, and in March it rose to 74.2. The amount of electricity production in January was 94.0, in February it was 93.2, and in March it was 95.2. The amount of automobile production in January was 41.0, in February it was 74.9, and in March it was 77.2. Its composite index rose from 78.6 on January 6 this year to 84.8 on March 17. This figure is indeed not as good as 99.0 in the summer of last year, but in terms of individual industrial sectors, such as the amount of freight transportation and the amount of automobile manufacturing, they are slightly higher than last year. Although the number of freight cars decreased from 604,137 on February 3 to 557,900 on April 7, this is a seasonal relationship. Because winter is over and summer is coming, the amount of coal used by the general public has decreased, so the number of freight cars has also decreased accordingly. We can see that electricity production, which is closely related to various industrial sectors and is also the most sensitive, increased from 1,636,000 kilowatt-hours in early February to 1,666,000 kilowatt-hours at the end of March. Furthermore, the amount of steel production is also sufficient to measure the situation of the US market. According to the figures released by the American Iron and Steel Association, the rate of steel production operations of all factories was 37.5% in early February, rose to 47.7% in early March, gradually decreased, and recently rose to 50.3%. The actual production numbers were 1,620,000 tons of pig iron produced in mid-March, an increase of 356,000 tons compared to the previous month. 2,797,000 tons of steel were produced in the same month, an increase of 572,000 tons compared to the previous month. In the first three months of this year, the total increase compared to the same period last year was 140% for pig iron and 131% for steel.

We all know that the United States is a car country and produces the most cars in the world. In January of this year, more than 160,700 cars were produced, in February more than 235,000 cars were produced, in March about 323,000 cars could be produced, and in April it is feared that it will approach 400,000 cars. Furthermore, the automobile industry has the most relationships with other sectors, such as the rubber industry, more than 80% of which is tied to the automobile industry. The volatile oil industry is also the same. Secondly, such as glass plates, nickel, aluminum, copper, and iron, and even copper, lead, hardwood, etc., are closely related to the automobile industry. Their future is determined by the prosperity or decline of the automobile industry. Therefore, the important position of the automobile industry can be inferred. Therefore, the general public is paying attention to this. Workers in automobile factories are even singing everywhere about the 36-hour work week and demanding a 20% wage increase. Not long ago, a national general strike was brewed, but it was fortunately quelled by the mediation of the President. But after all, it is only a temporary state. It is difficult to guarantee when it will break out again. What's more, labor unrest continues to exist and is brewing in the industrial areas of the United States. Therefore, the Roosevelt government is still seriously on guard. Given this tense domestic situation in the United States, the government is stepping up its guard for economic recovery. In terms of diplomacy, it is not only listed as secondary, but it also takes strength--economic strength--as the basis for determining its means of response. Although she still supports the open door policy, she is powerless to help others. (April 8th)

Jiangxi, Zhejiang, and Anhui Troops Encircle and Suppress Fang Zhimin's Band of Red Bandits. Red Bandit Fortifications are Destroyed One After Another. Hengfeng and Geyuan Can Be Taken Soon.

Nanchang Correspondence: Fang Zhimin's band of Red Bandits in northeastern Jiangxi is being surrounded and suppressed by large forces from the three provinces of Jiangxi, Zhejiang, and Anhui. The guerrilla tactics of advancing when we retreat and retreating when we advance, which were used in previous suppressions, are now completely inapplicable. The national army is advancing steadily, encircling and blocking, and has repeatedly achieved remarkable results. Therefore, the bandits are desperately building fortifications around Hengfeng and Geyuan, their base areas, and near the national army's positions, hoping to hold out. However, the troops of Yu Jishi have defeated the bandits in the areas north of Yushan, Shangrao, and Hengfeng, and the troops of Chen Diaoyuan in the north are also advancing on Hengbei from Dexing. The troops of Zhao Guantao in the south are also advancing north from Hekou and reached Laoyajian in Hengshu on the 25th of last month. There, the bandits' bogus 10th Army 83rd Regiment and bogus Independent Battalion had built solid bunkers in a dangerous location. Liang, the division commander of Zhao's troops, personally supervised the attack despite the rain. That day, there was heavy rain and dense fog. To avoid being ambushed, he first bombarded with artillery and then charged with infantry. At noon, he destroyed the bandits' earthen city outer trenches and approached the bunkers. Regiment Commander Zhang and Battalion Commander Wang supervised their troops to climb the bunkers and then broke through the bandits' bunkers. The bogus 83rd Regiment and bogus Independent Battalion guarding the bunkers were completely wiped out. Furthermore, after a certain division advancing west from Shangrao recovered Yangmei Mountain and Xiangu Mountain, people from the bandit area fled to Hekou and Shangrao in an endless stream. The division then advanced to Lengshui Keng, Diling Tou, Shengjia Fang, and other places in Hengshu. The bandit Fang once personally led the bandit masses to meet and resist, and there was a major battle in Longjing Wan. After the bandits were defeated and retreated, 400 bandit corpses were left on the battlefield. The above are all situations from the last ten days of last month. At the beginning of this month, the various armies have already advanced to the vicinity of Hengfeng and other places. According to news from the front, the national army recently captured Lianhe. The bandits' bogus Independent Battalion fled to Dayuan Wangjia, more than ten miles away in Huangsha Gang, with a total of 400 bandits and 300 guns, and are building fortifications. The bogus 10th Army fled to Huangteng Bridge south of Hengfeng County, the bogus 58th Regiment fled to the junction of Guixi and Qianshan, and the bogus Independent Regiment 59th Regiment fled back to the Zixi Shilong area at the junction of Qianshan and Chong'an in Fujian Province. The bogus 31st Division is composed of the old and weak who were forcibly conscripted from the bandit area and is being trained in the bogus Geyuan Province in northern Hengfeng. It cannot fight. In Shan Yali on the left wing of Geyuan, there is an arsenal that can only make earthen cannons. The bandit Fang was once injured and treated in the ninth district of Yiyang. The internal situation is extremely panicked. Bogus battalion commanders and below all want to surrender, but they have no chance. (May 8th)

Huainan Railway Construction Begins: Passing Through Hefei and Chaoxian to Wuhu Across the River

Wuhu Communication: The Huainan coal mine, exploited by the Construction Committee, has a vast mining area, abundant production, and excellent quality. The number of miners is no less than 20,000, producing six to seven hundred tons per day. Sales are widespread in the Yangtze River area, and most factories and ships in Wuhu also use it. However, the mining area is located in Jiulonggang and other places on the south bank of the Huai River, and inland transportation is inconvenient, making it extremely difficult to transport and sell to the Yangtze River. Therefore, the Huainan Railway is planned to be built, with the route starting from the mining area, passing through Hefei and Chaoxian, and reaching Yuxikou across the river from Wuhu. The design has already been finalized, and the entire line will be constructed in three sections for speed. The first section is from the mining area to Hefei, the second section is from Hefei to Chaoxian, and the third section is from Chaoxian to Yuxikou. The first section of the project has already started. Twelve hand-operated flatcars have recently been purchased in Wuhu for the use of working personnel to travel back and forth. (10th)

Catastrophic Defeat of Guangdong Silk Industry: Over 300 Silk Factories Closed in Shunde County, Losses of Tens of Millions of Dollars, Rural Economy Bankrupt, 200,000 Unemployed Female Workers, Most Emigrate

Guangzhou Correspondence: Shunde County's silk has always been a major export commodity of Guangdong Province. Silk factories are everywhere in the county, and there are many workers. Farmers have been engaged in sericulture for generations, and their families are well-off. The economic independence of their women is even the best in the province. However, in recent years, the Shunde silk industry has been affected by economic decline, and it has gradually declined from its heyday. Exports are scarce, resulting in the bankruptcy of the rural economy. According to statistics, Shunde County had 328 silk factories at its peak in 1925, but only eleven can maintain their business today. These few surviving silk factories are only supporting themselves for the time being by storing old silk. If the stored silk is sold out, it is still unknown whether they can continue to operate. However, according to statistics on the capital losses of the closed silk factories, it is already more than 18 million yuan. When the silk industry was prosperous, Shunde's financial activity was second to none in the province. During the annual silk transaction season, an average of 300,000 yuan was transported from Guangzhou to various parts of Shunde every day. This huge sum was the price paid by foreign merchants for ordering silk. The county had a monthly flow of cash of up to ten million yuan, circulating among each other. Not only did silk merchants make huge profits, but also hundreds of silver houses in Daliang, Chencun, Rongqi, Leliu, Shuiteng, and other places, specializing in remittance and mortgage businesses, benefited from the financial circulation. Recently, due to the sharp decline in silk exports, financial irregularities, and about seven out of ten silver houses have closed down accordingly. Since there is no market for silk and silk prices have plummeted, some families still raise silkworms, but the price they sell silk is less than one-tenth of the previous value, resulting in unbearable losses. In the past, the price of mulberry was ten yuan or five or six yuan per hundred catties, but now, because there is no market, it is only six or four corners per hundred catties. The income from mulberry is not enough to cover the labor cost. The county has more than 6,000 hectares of mulberry fields, producing more than ten dan of mulberry leaves per mu (100 catties per dan). Calculated at the current value, farmers have lost 30 million yuan. Currently, mulberry fields have been converted to planting miscellaneous grains, and mulberry gardens are completely bankrupt. Farmers in Shunde County account for half of the population, about 500,000, and there are about 270,000 female silk workers. Recently, due to the closure of silk factories and the abandonment of mulberry gardens, no less than 200,000 female workers have suddenly lost their jobs. These unemployed female workers are displaced and mostly go to cities to work as laborers. Recently, Nanyang has been recruiting female workers, and these women have turned to overseas. According to Hong Kong statistics, an average of two to three thousand female workers go to Singapore from Hong Kong every month. (May 4th)

Qingdao to Prepare for the Establishment of a Marine Biological Research Institute, Initiated by Zhang Xi, Director of the Peking Research Institute, and Others, and Drafted 14 Articles of the Research Institute's Regulations

Qingdao Correspondence: Zhang Xi, Director of the Peking Research Institute, Zeng Shengzhi, Professor of Shandong University, Jiang Bingran, Director of the Qingdao Observatory, Chen Zhen of Tsinghua University, Liu Chongyue of the Chinese Marine Biological Society, and five other biological experts believe that Qingdao has a mild climate and abundant aquatic products, is the center of the Yellow Sea and Bohai Sea fisheries, and has convenient land and water transportation, making it the most suitable place for researching marine organisms. Since the establishment of National Shandong University, it has spared no effort in the research and development of marine biology. However, it is not easy to concentrate talents, and teaching should seek more assistance. It is now planned to open the laboratory during the summer vacation period of various universities and research institutions to meet the needs of biological and aquatic experts from home and abroad to come to Qingdao for research. Moreover, the Qingdao Observatory Aquarium has relatively complete equipment, which is extremely convenient for mutual learning and observation. However, Shandong University's funding is stretched, and it is difficult to create independently. Therefore, it has jointly organized various universities and biological research institutions in the country to achieve this grand event. The drafted regulations and budget of the research institute are recorded below. "Regulations" 1. This institute is jointly organized by various universities and research institutions in the country to provide convenience for biologists to study and lecture on marine organisms. 2. This institute is located in Qingdao National Shandong University, and research rooms are also set up in the Qingdao Aquarium. 3. This institute has a committee, which is organized by one person sent by each university's biology department and research institution participating in it. 4. This institute has one director, who is elected by the committee. 5. The work of this institute is as follows: A. Provide convenience for various universities and research institutions to collect aquatic biological specimens. B. Provide convenience for various professors and experts to study marine organisms during the summer or usual times. C. Organize summer training courses. 6. The expenses of this institute are borne equally by each university and research institution participating in it. The annual fee for each university or institution is temporarily set at 600 yuan. 7. All schools and institutions participating in this institute, their professors, researchers, and students can enjoy the following benefits: (1) Use of the various laboratories and research rooms of this institute. (2) Use of the books and instruments of this institute. (3) Use of the tools for collecting and sorting specimens of this institute. (4) Use of the experimental drugs of this institute. (5) Use of the collection vessels of this institute. (6) Accommodation provided by this institute. (7) Admission to the summer training courses. Items 4 to 7 are only applicable during the summer vacation period. Collection expenses for other places are self-provided. 8. The committee holds a meeting once every summer vacation to review the following matters: A. Review the budget proposal. B. Review the work report. C. Discuss and decide on important plans and equipment. D. Raise funds and allocate their use. E. Revise the regulations. 9. The powers of the director are as follows: A. Manage all routine affairs of this institute. B. Prepare the budget and final accounts and the annual report, and distribute them to the participating universities and research institutions. C. Implement the resolutions of the committee meeting. 10. When teachers and students of various universities or institutions joining this institute come to the institute to collect and research, they must bring a certificate letter for reference, except for the members of this institute. If there are a large number of people, a list must also be prepared and notified in advance. 11. Students participating in the collection at the institute are limited to third and fourth-year students of the biology department. Each university shall not exceed 15 people per session. 12. Personnel from universities or institutions that have not joined the research institute will not be entertained when they come to the institute for research or collection without the permission of the committee. 13. This institute does not provide accommodation or vessels for the personnel who are specially allowed to come to the institute for research and collection in the preceding paragraph. The method of paying fees will be determined separately. 14. The measures for the summer training courses will be determined separately. "Budget" A new mobile seawater fish farming room will be built in the Qingdao Aquarium, 1,500 yuan. Five hundred yuan for orange tables, etc. in the research room upstairs in the Aquarium. Nine hundred yuan for refrigerators. Rent a sea cucumber boat for collecting at sea (for two months), 400 yuan. Rent a steamship to collect in various places in Jiaozhou Bay (for two months), 600 yuan. Four hundred yuan for collection equipment. Seven hundred yuan for summer training course expenses. The total is 5,000 yuan. (11th)

Songjiang: Bribery Case of Supervisory Official Judged

Yang Shaoxian, a former supervisory official of the Public Security Bureau, was ordered to go to Wang's in Zhalin at the end of last year to investigate a robbery case. Relying on his duties, he accused the victim of smoking opium and took the opportunity to demand bribes from the victim. After being robbed, the victim had no cash at home and hired a boat to borrow from relatives and friends. The supervisory official suddenly thought of smoking opium in the boat and ordered the boatman Wang Xiaotao to buy it. When passing through the territory of Fengxian County, he was seized by the Fengyi police and escorted to the county. Then, this county prepared a document to welcome and bring him back for interrogation by the county court. Now, after repeated trials by the criminal court of the court, the facts have been clarified. On the afternoon of the 10th, a proposal was announced and the defendant Yang Shaoxian was sentenced to four months of imprisonment for the crime of using his position to solicit bribes, and fined 200 yuan for smoking opium, to be executed concurrently. Wang Xiaotao was fined 20 yuan for helping to smoke opium. Wang Lu (the victim)'s trial proceedings were suspended. The defendant Yang Shaoxian declared in court that he was dissatisfied and was ordered to be returned to custody.

Now, Zhang Ruoshui and others, chairman of the Rice Industry Board of Directors, have telegraphed to Chairman Chen of the Provincial Government, Director Yu of the Department of Civil Affairs, and Director Shen of the Department of Construction, requesting that the county government be ordered to open the undredged dam immediately to avoid disputes. The original telegram is as follows: Chen, Chairman of the Zhenjiang Provincial Government, Yu, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, Shen, Director of the Department of Construction, Jun Jian: The general meeting on the 30th decided to end the east section due to the mildew season and busy farming, and to suspend dredging of the west section to avoid the depletion of the middle section. The tide is not flowing. It is suspected that the farmers are demanding more than 4,000 yuan based on inside information. The delay is intentional. Who will be responsible if a riot occurs? Please telegraph the county government to open the undredged dam immediately to comply with the resolution and avoid disputes. Suzhou: Minor Case Reveals No Injuries

Xu Yongliang's eight-year-old son, Xiaodi, of No. 14 Jiudao Lane, was beaten by Huang Yanren, a ten-year-old apprentice in the Hanzhen Carving Shop, and died of serious injuries the day before yesterday. Xu Yongliang reported the case to the district and summoned Huang Yanren to the bureau for interrogation. It is now learned that the District Procuratorate sent Inspector Xia to conduct an examination at 4 pm on the 14th. During the examination, it was found that Xu Xiaodi had no injuries. The cause of death was that Xu Xiaodi had been suffering from fever for several days and was coated with raw gypsum by the doctor. Xiaodi was weak, causing the fever to invade the inside and die. The young suspect Huang Yanren confessed to the Public Security Bureau that he only admitted pushing Xiaodi down and did not kick him. The bureau has transferred Huang Yanren to the District Procuratorate for investigation yesterday (11th).

Suicide in Suzhou After Speculation Failure

Internal Strife Among the Initiators of Sumu Road

Yi people Liu Fuqing and others initiated investment in the construction of the road and have been approved by the Department of Construction for record. They are now planning the project and will start construction next month. However, news came that a major change had occurred among the initiators. Yesterday (11th), Xu Huangen and others, initiators of the road from Wuxi, submitted a report to the county government, stating that at the beginning of the Sumu Road project, the fixed capital was 100,000 yuan, of which 70,000 yuan was for the purchase of buses, which was the responsibility of Xu, and 30,000 yuan was for the construction of the road, of which Xu was responsible for seven-tenths and Liu was responsible for three-tenths. However, Liu actually assumed the position of chief representative of the initiators and controlled everything. If they were asked to withdraw, they would use the filing as a threat. Moreover, Liu did not meet the qualifications of the initiator. It is now planned to cooperate with Shanghai merchant Xia Yongfu to handle it. Please allow Liu Fuqing to withdraw in order to facilitate the progress and maintain road administration.

Wuxi: Two Cases of Murder of Men and Women

Zhu Yunzhang, nicknamed Ala, a 43-year-old villager of Zhu Erfang Bridge Township near Meicun Town in the Twelfth District, was strong and skilled in martial arts. On the 9th of this month, Yunzhang went to A'er's house in Qifangwan to attend a society wine. He returned home late at night. Unexpectedly, he suddenly encountered five or six enemies on the way, who stabbed Yunzhang's legs more than ten times with sharp knives. His waist, back, and abdomen were also stabbed several times. He died instantly. Seeing that their goal had been achieved, the murderers carried the body to the wheat field bank at the Zhu Erfang Bridge. The next day, someone discovered it and reported it to Lu Yuquan, the head of the 566th district, and the deceased's wife, Chen, who came to the city to report to the District Procuratorate. Inspector Ren led officials to the countryside on a wheel at 7 am yesterday (11th) to examine the body. It was confirmed that he died from knife wounds sustained during his lifetime. After the examination, he ordered the family of the deceased to prepare a coffin and wait for the arrest of the murderer to be dealt with according to the law. In addition, a nameless female corpse was found at about 5 am yesterday morning in the Xiaocao River, Xie Chen Lane, Shuangchedu, near the 113th district of Luoshe Town in the Sixteenth District. The corpse was lying face down, with the upper half of the body submerged in the river. Only the legs and buttocks were placed on the shore. One foot was shoeless, taken off on the right bank. There were traces of people trampling on the weeds on the shore. Several mulberry tree branches were also broken. There were messy footprints on the ground and prints of the head pressed into the mud, as well as several hairs left behind. It seemed that she had been murdered. Chen Huiquan, the head of the district, came to the city to report to the District Procuratorate. Inspector Ren led officials to the countryside to examine the body.

They were all taken to the bureau and transferred to the local branch court for legal action.

He immediately ordered the survey team to comply. In the early morning of the day before, the team measured a branch of the poplar tree that was obstructing the area near Wanxiang. Unexpectedly, villagers Wan Arong and others came out to stop them and beat the surveyors, including Tang, for a while. The order was chaotic. Among them, worker Yu Hanzhen was surrounded by the crowd and beaten with fists and feet. He was covered in bruises and collapsed on the ground, unconscious. Changshu: Rice Merchants Suffer Losses After Changing Measures

Since the unified measurement of rice measures in the county on the 5th of last month, it has been a month so far. Unexpectedly, the hidden losses have been quite large. The new measures have been changed, but they have not yet been unified everywhere. For example, Wuxi and other places have not yet implemented them. However, a group of rural rice sellers are unaware of the use of the new measures and mostly go to Wuxi to sell or purchase rice. As a result, rice merchants here have suffered a lot of losses. Therefore, they have jointly petitioned the county government, requesting that the Department of Construction be notified to quickly order the counties in Wuxi to quickly change to the new measures to maintain commercial transportation. After receiving the report, the county government specially drafted a telegram on the 10th to代电建县, requesting to quickly order Wuxi to change to the new measures to maintain commercial profits.

(2) According to the prison warden's report, the rations for the detention center in April exceeded the quota by 17.8 yuan. (3) The local budget for the 23rd year has been approved, and the revenue and expenditure are appropriate, totaling 942,200 yuan. Jiangyin: Militia Member Beats a Village Woman to Death

Her aunt reported to the Local Militia, who took Zheng to the militia headquarters. Suddenly, she died. According to training officer Qian Jing and squad leader Huang Shenggen, she went to the kitchen to eat and returned from the drill. Zheng was缠绕with a trouser belt around her head and勒死 herself. After Cao's examination, it was confirmed that the deceased Zheng had a bruise behind her right ear and fatal bleeding from the ear. The belt on her neck was纏绕after death. It was confirmed that she had been beaten to death. After the examination, Qian Jingshan and others from the militia headquarters were questioned. They all claimed that they did not know the cause of death. When questioned the doorman Mi Jindai, he only knew that Zhang Zheng wanted food and ordered her to take it from the kitchen. How she died was unknown. The question officer asked when the militiamen were drilling and when the deceased died. They replied that they were drilling at 3 pm and the deceased died at about 2 pm. The questioning officer believed that Qian Jingshan and others claimed that Zheng had died when they returned from the drill, which was completely an excuse. Jiashan Economic Oppression Leads to Three Suicides

This county has always been known as a prosperous land. In recent years, commerce has drastically declined, and the rural economy has become extremely bankrupt. As a result, incidents of people committing suicide due to economic oppression have been occurring daily. For example, on the 9th, in the southern section of Fish Bridge in the town, a child bride named Xiao Bao, disliking the difficult life and constantly quarreling with her aunt, hanged herself. Also, a woman surnamed Wang from Yangmiao Town, who married a man surnamed Yao in Jiaxing, was left destitute after her husband's death. On the 11th, she committed suicide by taking poison. Yu Liqing, who ran a sundry stall in Youdonggang Town, had a mother and wife. He fell ill last year and was burdened with debt. Taking advantage of his family's unpreparedness, he hanged himself. Funds for his coffin and burial were entirely donated by philanthropists. His elderly mother and widowed wife, fearing they would not be able to survive in the future, also plan to follow him to the underworld. The tragic economic situation in this county can be seen from this.

Hangzhou New Cocoons from Various Counties in Zhejiang Province to be Marketed

The silkworm rearing season in Zhejiang Province has been affected by the frequent changes in weather, such as cold spells, warm spells, sunny days, and rainy days. The results of native silkworm breeds are not ideal. However, improved breeds are hatching later, and their physical condition is stronger. Especially in counties such as Xiao, Shao, Hang, Sheng, Wuxing, Jiaxing, Haiyan, Haining, Lin'an, Changxing, Wukang, Fuyang, and Zhuji, where model improvements have been implemented, sufficient disinfection and rational artificial hatching, joint rearing of young silkworms, and widespread guidance have been provided. Therefore, human effort has been able to compensate for the shortcomings of nature. According to a survey by the Construction Department, the early batches in various districts have already completed their fourth molt, and those with later leafing are also around their third molt. The overall progress has been good. New cocoons will be available for sale after the 20th of this month. It is estimated that 600,000 sheets of improved silkworm eggs were distributed to various districts during the spring season. With unified breeds, there will be a significant harvest. Furthermore, after the amendment of the Zhejiang Province Management Regulations for Collecting Cocoons and Controlling Cocoon Dealers, all parties are satisfied. Cocoon merchants have been registering with the Construction Department. However, the silk market has not shown any improvement recently. In the future, the price of cocoons may only be around twenty cents per catty.

Near Zhoujiasha in Ganpu, on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway, at 3 PM yesterday, a woman surnamed Zhang, the daughter-in-law of Su Tianshun, a farmer from Sujiadai, was passing by while shopping when a small chartered car speeding from Shanghai to Hangzhou suddenly appeared. The woman hurriedly dodged into the reeds on the side of the road. Unexpectedly, the driver's driving skills were poor, and he also drove into the reeds, knocking Zhang down and causing her to faint. Her waist and legs were severely injured. Seeing that he had caused an accident, the driver sped away. Fortunately, villagers witnessed the incident and carried her to the hospital for treatment. A telegram was sent to the Haining station to detain the vehicle involved in the accident for investigation.

Local News

New Coins of the 23rd Year of the Republic Central Mint Has Begun Minting The Review Committee Held its 13th Regular Meeting Yesterday Chen Xing, Acting Chairman, Reported on the Work

The Review Committee of the Central Mint held its 13th regular meeting at the Central Bank at 4:30 PM yesterday. The Chemical Examination Office and the Secretariat reported on their work. The minting of the new coins of the 23rd year of the Republic has begun. Details are as follows:

The members of the Review Committee present at the regular meeting included Mai Kai, Xu Xinliu, Shi Ying, Xue Laideng, Xi Demao, Chen Jian'an, Ye Fuxiao, Ye Zhuotang, Lin Shu, Wu Yunzhai, Ma Xier, Shi Demen, Lai Na, Shi Dujin, and others. Those present as observers included Lu Xuepu, Director of the Central Mint; Wei Jingzhou, Deputy Director; Wei Tingtao, Director of the General Affairs Department; Ge Laide, Chemical Examiner of the Review Committee; and Qiao Fusan, Secretary. Chairman Kong Yongzhi was away from Shanghai on official business and was temporarily replaced by Committee Member Chen Jian'an. Li Zechang recorded the meeting.

Work Report The chairman announced the opening of the meeting and the minutes of the previous meeting were approved. Secretary Qiao Fusan reported that new coins worth 5.5 million yuan were certified in April. 5,061 Type B factory bars (880 fineness) were also supervised and stamped. He also gave a detailed report on the work situation in the meeting in April. Subsequently, the chemical examiner reported that the average fineness of the new coins examined in April was 880.06, which is 0.06 higher than the legal standard. The weight was 26.6962 grams, which is about three ten-thousandths lower than the legal weight, all within the legal tolerance. The 5,061 Type B factory bars (880 fineness) were also supervised and stamped with the committee's stamp when their fineness marks were checked, according to regulations. The meeting adjourned at 5:30 PM.

Minting of New Coins The Central Mint began using the new coin molds of the 23rd year of the Republic on May 7. The design of the new coins is the same as that of the new coins of the 22nd year of the Republic, except that the year "22" has been changed to "23." The Review Committee of the Central Mint has also changed the certificate numbers for the new coins certified each day, starting from number one on May 8. The mark "(23)" has been added before each of these certificate numbers to indicate the distinction, and the Central Bank has been requested to forward this information to all silver and money businesses.

Hu Yunzhuang Injured in Horse Fall in Lanzhou Flew to Shanghai Yesterday Dr. Niu Huilin Consulted Recovery Expected in Four to Five Weeks

Hu Yunzhuang, manager of the Deutsch-Asiatische Bank, was unfortunately injured in a horse fall in Lanzhou on the 6th while accompanying Song Ziwen, Standing Committee Member of the Economic Commission, on an inspection tour of the Northwest. Bone setting surgery will be performed within a few days, and he is expected to recover in about four to five weeks. Papal Representative to China Archbishop Zanin Scheduled to Go to Beijing to Meet Chairman Lin to Present Papal Award

According to Xin Sheng She, Archbishop Zanin, the second Papal Representative to China, arrived in Shanghai. The day before yesterday, he presented a gold medal to Lu Bohong. Yesterday, Mayor Wu Tiecheng went to return the visit. Today, the National Catholic Action Association broadcasted a welcome program. Yesterday, a grand mass was held in Xujiahui. On the 14th, he will go to Beijing to pay respects to the foreign affairs authorities and meet Chairman Lin. On the 19th, various government agencies and public organizations in the city will jointly host a banquet. Details are as follows:

Mayor Returns Visit

After Archbishop Zanin paid a visit to Mayor Wu the day before yesterday, the mayor scheduled a return visit for yesterday. At 9:00 AM yesterday morning, Lu Bohong, president of the National Catholic Action Association, and his son, Lu Yigeng, went to the downtown area to greet the mayor. The mayor, accompanied by secretaries Geng Jiaji and Tang Shixuan, went to Xujiahui Cathedral to return the visit to the representative. Zanin, along with representatives from the Papal Delegation to China, Bishop An Chongyi, and Bishop Hui of the Jiangsu region, welcomed them into the living room. They shook hands as a greeting and talked for more than two minutes before Wu took his leave.

Presentation of Medal

Archbishop Zanin, at the invitation of members of the Catholic Action Association in various districts of Shanghai, held a grand mass at Xin Puyu Hall outside the South Gate the night before last. At noon, the Catholic Action Association of various districts hosted a banquet for Zanin. During the banquet, President Lu Bohong delivered a welcome speech, expressing his gratitude and stating that he was fortunate to have good guidance and vowed to work hard under the leadership of Catholicism. Zanin replied, praising Lu for his efforts for Catholicism and the country, his charitable deeds, his relief of the poor, and his contributions to society. The Pope has long heard of his reputation and is very pleased. He is now awarding Lu a gold medal to commemorate his sixtieth birthday, as a sign of recognition. He also presented him with his autographed photograph to express his gratitude for his warm welcome and hospitality. According to reports, the Papal Gold Medal is awarded to heads of state and ambassadors from various countries. This time, when Archbishop Zanin came to China, the Pope gave him two gold medals to bring, one for Chairman Lin and one for Lu Bohong.

Grand Mass Held

In the morning, Archbishop Zanin held a grand mass at Xujiahui Cathedral. At 11:00 AM, he went to the welcome meeting of the Xujiahui Middle School Alumni Association. The Supervision Office of the National Catholic Action Association will broadcast a welcome program at the Guohua Radio Station from 4:00 PM to 5:00 PM today (the 12th). All reports will be in Mandarin to allow Catholic friends across the country to listen. Today is also the Pope's name day, so there will be a speech commemorating the Pope. The program is as follows: (1) National Anthem, (2) Report on the purpose of the broadcast, (3) Play the Papal March (Quartet), (4) Announce Archbishop Zanin's resume, (5) Sing a welcome song, (6) Read a welcome speech in Mandarin, (7) Sing "Thou Art Peter", (8) Read welcome speeches in ten languages: Latin, Greek, Italian, French, English, Russian, German, Spanish, Portuguese, and Esperanto (Harmonica interlude), (9) Sing "Pius Pastor Bonus", (10) Report news, (11) Commemorate the Pope, (12) "King of Kings" song, (13) Commemorate the former Papal Representative to China, Archbishop Celso Costantini, (14) Play music.

Scheduled Trip to Beijing

Archbishop Zanin has changed his schedule to take the train to Beijing on the 14th instead of the 13th, which is a Sunday, to pay respects to Minister of Foreign Affairs Wang Zhengting, meet with Chairman Lin of the National Government, present his credentials, and present the gold medal awarded by the Pope. He will then leave Beijing for Shanghai.

Public Banquet by Various Circles

Mayor Wu Tiecheng of Shanghai and various government agencies and public organizations in the city will host a public banquet for Archbishop Zanin at the Zhengxiu Middle School Auditorium on the 19th to show their welcome.

A large number of ships are being dispatched to rush the loading. All are being unloaded at the China Merchants Bureau warehouse in Pudong.

Flour to Shanghai There are 25 tons of flour in the contract. Last time, China found that the sale of wheat flour domestically was not suitable, and the losses were greater than with wheat. Therefore, we had discussed with the United States, but there was no result. Now, less than 1,000 tons of the wheat flour in this item has been shipped to Shanghai. The bulk of the flour is also scheduled to begin shipping from the United States to China this month. The first batch is expected to arrive in late this month.

Statistics on Chinese Goods Exported to the United States in April

According to the Da Mei Evening News, the US Consul-General in Shanghai announced that the total value of goods exported from Shanghai to the United States in April was US$1,131,000. The total for the first four months of this year is US$4,849,915. The largest category of exports to the United States in April was inedible animals and animal products, totaling approximately US$779,189. The total value of this type of goods exported to the United States in four months was US$3,153,258, accounting for more than half of the total value of all exports to the United States. Textiles were the second largest category, totaling US$1,395,261 in four months, with US$258,907 in April. Non-metallic minerals totaled US$71,166 in four months, with US$55,038 in April. In addition, the value of jade products exported to the United States in April was US$44,395. The remaining categories ranged from tens of thousands to thousands of dollars. The total value of goods exported from Shanghai to the Philippines in April was US$91,028. The total for the first four months of this year is US$452,399. Exports to Hawaii were only worth US$4,565 in April, and the total for the four months was US$16,470.

Cotton Control Commission Requests Exemption from Yarn, Cloth Tax; Ministry of Finance Rejects as Impractical

The National Economic Council's Cotton Control Commission, to alleviate difficulties in the yarn and cloth industry, had requested the Ministry of Finance to exempt it from business tax. News has arrived from Shanghai that the Ministry of Finance has rejected the request as impractical. The original response stated: "Regarding your commission's letter requesting a general order to all provinces and cities to exempt the yarn and cloth industry from business tax, which is currently under consideration, a subsequent letter was received from the Jinan Chengtong Textile Company stating that Japanese yarn merchants along the Jiaoji Railway are unaffected by business tax, severely impacting Chinese yarn. Please consider the previous letter concurrently." The Ministry notes its deep concern for the difficulties faced by domestic industries due to lagging production and business stagnation. Previously, a method was approved to exempt cotton raw material purchases by yarn factories from business tax, and orders were issued to all provinces and cities to comply. Subsequently, a letter was received from the Executive Yuan's secretariat, forwarding a request from the Shanghai Flour Mill Association to legally prohibit various provincial finance departments from collecting business tax from flour mills' branch offices. It was deemed feasible to exempt branch offices only engaged in sales and liaison from business tax. A clear explanation of this exemption was issued to provincial and municipal governments. Considering the foregoing, a blanket exemption for yarn and cloth business tax is practically unfeasible. Enclosed is document No. 4381 for your reference."

Korean Red Ginseng Imports Surge, According to International Trade Bureau Statistics

Yesterday, Ji Zejin, director of the guidance department of the International Trade Bureau, stated that red ginseng has traditionally been the top import from Korea. After the September 18th Incident, the sales of Korean red ginseng plummeted. Mitsui Bussan Kaisha's red ginseng export trade nearly ceased, and the product piled up in the Kaesong production area. White ginseng production was increased for consumption by Japanese and Koreans, causing its price to plummet. Red ginseng was only exported in small quantities to Taiwan, Southeast Asia, and the Northeast. Although occasional imports occurred through Tianjin, Qingdao, and Shanghai, the numbers were minimal. According to statistics from the Monopoly Bureau, Mitsui Bussan Kaisha, the export volume of Korean red ginseng in mid-March of last year was 590 catties (total for China, Southeast Asia, and Taiwan). The total export volume last year was approximately 26,000 catties, of which China accounted for 1,470 catties. However, recent statistics show Korean red ginseng exports at 4,480 catties, a sharp increase of 3,961 catties compared to the same period last year. Of this, China accounts for 385 catties, Taiwan 600 catties, and Southeast Asia over 490 catties, demonstrating that China is the primary market for Korean red ginseng.

Jianghai Customs Launches Two New Ships; Bottle-Breaking Ceremony Forgone Amid National Crisis; Completion Expected by End of Month

The Jianghai Customs' newly built patrol ships, Wenxing and Yunxing, at the Jiangnan Shipbuilding Yard, have seen rapid progress since their keel laying last year. Due to the installation of the engines prior to the launch, the ceremony was delayed until 10:00 AM yesterday. Attendees included Chen Zaofan, deputy director of the Jiangnan Shipbuilding Yard, business director Yu Jianfu, statistics director Ye Fangzhe, security chief Ye Baoqi, representatives from Jianghai Customs, and officers from the First Fleet of the Navy.

Launch Details

Due to the national crisis, the traditional bottle-breaking ceremony was forgone as a cost-saving measure. During the launch, the Wenxing was first to enter the Huangpu River at high tide, completing the process in five minutes. The Yunxing followed suit. After the launch, two small vessels dispatched by the yard towed the patrol ships to the yard's wharf.

Ship Specifications

The patrol ships built by Jianghai Customs at the yard previously include Dexing, Lianxing, Hexing, Haiping, Haiyan, and Haian. According to a spokesperson from the yard, the two ships have a displacement of 700 tons, a length of 140 feet, a width of 32 feet, a depth of 11 feet 6 inches, a draft of 10 feet, and a speed of 13 knots per hour. The internal equipment is entirely modern, and completion is expected by the end of June.

The focus is on improving agriculture itself, promoting key aspects of cultivation, improving agricultural tools, and raising livestock, with the goal of revitalizing agriculture and promoting disaster prevention.

Chamber of Commerce Urges Straw Hat Industry to Improve Products; Standardize Sizes and Styles to Compete in International Markets

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent a letter to the Straw and Felt Hat Industry Association, stating: "We are forwarding a letter from Mr. Yu of Yongxing Foreign Firm, outlining a meeting to discuss various issues to promote the hat industry and achieve positive results. The industry is linked to the livelihood of millions of Chinese people, and unless careful improvements are made to meet foreign demand, the industry will inevitably decline sharply. Currently, most hat exporters face similar challenges, particularly the need to strictly adhere to required styles. Our firm has been operating in China for over 50 years, and we are a major hat buyer in Java and Italy, with branches in both locations. Our Paris headquarters holds a significant position in the industry and has access to accurate style reports. We propose to collaborate with major Chinese export firms and request the association's assistance in advising and encouraging local weavers to avoid misguided practices. We believe the straw hat industry in China has the potential for significant growth, provided that workers are willing to listen to advice and be compliant. If workers can produce perfect work, they will receive better compensation. The greatest difficulty is that hat-weaving villages are not fully meeting the needs of foreign hat buyers. We suggest that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce or relevant foreign trade organizations send government personnel to promote awareness in rural villages, ensuring that buyers are satisfied. Neighboring Japan has made significant progress in its work and business practices over the past 30 years to gain a foothold in the market, serving as a precedent. If our export merchants can guarantee accurate sizes and styles, as Japanese merchants do, they will also be welcomed by buyers. We have sent a similar letter to the Foreign Trade Department of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, hoping to promote the interests of China and the industry for positive results." An English copy of the letter is attached for your reference.

Jiangsu Provincial Farmers' Bank Plans Shanghai Branch

The Jiangsu Provincial Government, to regulate rural finance and support rural production, established the Jiangsu Provincial Farmers' Bank in 1927. After seven or eight years of effort, it has accumulated over 3 million yuan in capital, 300,000 yuan in public reserve funds, and over 30 branch offices. Since Zhao Dihua, Director of the Finance Department, also became General Manager last year, efforts to consolidate have been intensified. Chairman Chen Guofu recognizes the need to expand the bank. A recent decision was made to allocate an additional 700,000 yuan, which is expected to be paid in full soon. The bank's main businesses include managing warehouses, promoting rural production and marketing cooperatives, and supporting other agricultural organizations. In Jiangsu Province, there are currently over 60 warehouses and over 1,400 cooperatives, with deposits exceeding 4 million yuan and loans exceeding 3 million yuan. During this time of rural economic hardship, the 30 million farmers in Jiangsu see the bank as a savior. However, with so many farmers in need, the several million yuan in funds are insufficient to meet demand. The bank's authorities believe it is necessary to establish a branch in Shanghai, a center of capital and a financial hub, to balance rural and urban finance. To promote the sale of inland agricultural products in cities, the bank will attach a provincial agricultural product sales office to the Shanghai branch, which is currently being prepared. The branch has been located at 275 Minkuo Road, Xin Kaihe, and is scheduled to open on the 25th of this month. Wu Rencang, Deputy Manager of the head office, is in Shanghai actively preparing. It is rumored that after the interior is completed, the branch will actively liaise with the Shanghai financial community.

Public Works Department Open-Air Swimming Pool to Open on May 15th

The Public Works Department's open-air swimming pool on Jiangwan Road is scheduled to open on May 15th, with the following regulations: 1. The pool will be open from 6:00 AM to 8:00 PM daily, except on Wednesdays and Sundays, when it will be reserved for women and children from 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM. 2. Admission is 40 cents per day, except on Saturdays, Sundays, and Public Works Department holidays, when it is 50 cents. 3. Children under 12 years of age must be accompanied by a responsible adult. 4. Anyone showing signs of infectious disease will not be admitted. 5. Women and children with long hair must wear a suitable swimming cap. 6. Swimmers must shower before entering the pool and wear appropriate swimwear. 7. Spitting is prohibited in the pool and at the entrance. 8. Personal belongings, including swimwear, towels, and valuables, may be entrusted to the pool attendant, but the pool is not responsible for loss or damage. 9. The PWD is not responsible for injuries sustained by those using the pool. 10. Alcoholic beverages are not permitted. 11. Disorderly or indecent behavior is prohibited. 12. Violators of these regulations will be immediately ejected. 13. The PWD reserves the right to refuse admission to anyone. Private groups may rent the pool for private use in the evenings. The fee is 40 yuan for the hours of 9:00 PM to 11:00 PM and 50 yuan for the hours of 9:00 PM to midnight. The fees cover up to 100 people, with an additional 40 cents per person exceeding that limit. For rental inquiries or other questions, please contact the Public Works Department office at 223 Hankou Road, Room 127, telephone 12410, extension 26.

Postal Employee Accused of Embezzlement

Ge Suizhi, 41, a native of Ningbo, residing at No. 88, Hongfu Lane, Xinchan Road, has been an employee of the Postal General Bureau on North Sichuan Road for 19 years. He currently works in the parcel department, responsible for collecting and disbursing funds on behalf of customers. For the past three years, he has been accused of altering parcel postage amounts for embezzlement. After investigators reported to the director of the bureau, it was found that out of the 5,000 yuan he handled daily, 153.545 yuan was missing, and a single payment slip from Kaifeng was altered from 13 yuan to 413 yuan. In addition, the amounts on twenty cargo card slips were also altered. On the day before yesterday, the Hongkou Police Station, led by Chinese Detective Zhu Jihuang, secretly arrested Ge with a court warrant. The evidence was brought to the police station, and yesterday morning, he was brought before the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. PWD lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that the defendant completely denied the charges at the police station and requested a postponement for further investigation. The evidence card slips were presented for inspection. The defendant admitted to working at the bureau for 19 years and currently earning 300 yuan per month, but denied altering any amounts on the card slips. He hired lawyer Fan Gang to represent him and requested bail. Zhang Yaoshu, an investigator from the bureau, and Zhang William, an accountant, testified about the situation. Judge Xiao Xiefei ordered Ge to provide a security of 2,000 yuan and adjourned the hearing to investigate further.

Yesterday, the police transferred two servants from the gambling den, Zhang Yongchang (38 years old, Suzhou native) and Xia Dongji (33 years old, Ningbo native), to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District. Police lawyer Gu Shouxi stated that the police investigation was ongoing and requested a postponement. Judge Wu Fanglian examined Zhang and Xia briefly and adjourned the hearing to the 15th. The defendants were returned to custody.

Beacon of the Black Sea

The harm of opium is universally known. Those addicted to it neglect their work, ruin their families, and even sell their wives and children to continue the habit. The smoke from cooking can be cut off, but the black smoke [of opium] cannot be absent. As a result, many sink into the lower classes and commit crimes. Such people are the dregs of the family, the waste of society, and the parasites of the nation. Recently, Chen Guofu, Chairman of Jiangsu Province, reported during a joint Party-Government memorial week that there are at least one or two hundred thousand opium smokers in the province. The actual number is likely several times higher. If this continues, the disaster of national destruction and racial extinction will be imminent. In fact, not only knowledgeable people deeply detest it, viewing it as a flood or ferocious beast, but also smokers themselves deeply feel the pain. However, perhaps due to physical weakness or financial constraints, they have not found a good way to quit for a while, and thus are immersed in a sea of suffering, unable to escape. It is truly lamentable. Now, fortunately, there is Dr. Lai Gongliang, who, based on his rich experience and precise research, has established the Tegong Jian Opium Addiction Hospital at 208 Baker Road (telephone 9512). He guarantees absolutely no pain and complete abstinence in the shortest period. Patients can also be cured at the same time. Furthermore, he aims to save people and charges very low fees. The poor are charged only for the cost of medicine. This is truly an excellent opportunity for wronged souls in the black registry to see the light of day again. Currently, the hospital is helping many people quit bad habits every day. Everyone praises Dr. Lai's benevolent heart and skillful art, which is said to be unique in Shanghai.

Central Bank Inspection Report

The 196th Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserves of the Central Bank states: "In accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this association is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the issuance of convertible banknotes by this bank. The 196th inspection was conducted at the bank's issuance office on May 10, 1934. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) Total amount of convertible banknotes issued: 69,022,208 silver dollars, including 62,574,771 silver dollar banknotes and 6,447,437 subsidiary coin banknotes. The total amount of convertible banknote reserves is 69,022,208 silver dollars, including 55,976,208 silver dollars in cash reserves. This cash reserve is stored in the bank's issuance treasury (52,524,895 silver dollars), in branches in various ports (1,659,234 silver dollars), and in other banks (1,792,079 silver dollars). The guaranteed reserve is equivalent to 13,046,000 silver dollars. (B) Total amount of Customs Gold Unit convertible banknotes issued: 373,324.7 Customs Gold Units. The total amount of Customs Gold Unit convertible banknote reserves is 373,324.7 Customs Gold Units, including 7,351 taels, 9 mace, and 5 fen of silver, valued at 50779, equivalent to 373,324.7 Customs Gold Units. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guaranteed reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guaranteed reserve is less than 40%, which is consistent with the regulations. This report is hereby made. May 11, 1934. Li Fuxun, Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank; Supervisors: Xie Mingxun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiyin."

Architectural Association Sends Representatives to Beiping to Observe and Seek to Develop Eastern Inherent Art

The Shanghai Architectural Association, in view of the fact that modern architectural projects in our country tend to be Westernized, not only obliterating the inherent architectural art of the East, but also causing countless amounts of money to flow abroad each year for imported building materials, believes that improvements should be made to promote Eastern architectural art. Among the architectural arts in the East, our country is the best, and Beiping, the old capital, should be regarded as the most important. Therefore, the association has specially sent Du Yangen, Liu Jiasheng, Du Junxiong, and others to Beiping by car at 8 o'clock yesterday morning to visit the architecture of the Forbidden City and collect materials, so that our inherent magnificent palace-style architecture can be combined with economical and practical Western methods to create a modern, economical, and practical new type of architecture. At the same time, after the representatives arrive in Beiping, they will also discuss architectural academics with Zhu Qiqian, the president of the Chinese Construction Society, and Wang Shen, the director of the Beiping Municipal Engineering Bureau. It is heard that the duration of this visit is set for one month, after which they will return to Shanghai.

Red Pill King of Pudong, Clever Methods of the Honorable Girl, Trading Through Holes in the Bamboo Fence—Reputation Spread and Finally Cracked—

The poisonous atmosphere of red pills permeates all of Shanghai. Although the police have repeatedly cracked down and investigated severely, they continue to rise and fall, and have never been completely eradicated. There is an old woman from Tongzhou, Jiang Zhu, who is nearly fifty years old, nicknamed "Honorable Girl." She has a daughter named Lin Ying, who is only fourteen years old. The mother and daughter live together at No. 2 Lane 90, Dongchang Road, Lan Nidu, Pudong, secretly establishing an agency for selling red pill drugs. Her sales methods are extremely secretive. It is said that buyers cannot directly go to her house to purchase red pills. Honorable Girl needs to tear a small hole in the bamboo fence near the bottom of Renji Lane behind her house as a place for transactions. Her daughter Lin Ying is in charge of all drug and money transactions. Therefore, those who are not experienced in this way cannot ask for help. The business is prosperous and the profits are abundant. However, it was soon noticed by outsiders, so the momentum became huge. Local people praised her as the "Red Pill King of Pudong." Recently, it was detected by Lu Ying, the chief of the third district of the Municipal Public Security Bureau and the detective team. He sent people to guard there every day. Sure enough, at about 3 p.m. the day before yesterday, when the detectives and policemen were checking pedestrians at the intersection of Dongchang Road, they suddenly saw two middle-aged men coming in a hurry, looking suspicious. They immediately went forward to search and found a bag of red pills on them on the spot. After taking them to the district for questioning, they confessed that one was Zhu Helin, 33 years old, from Hankou, living at No. 38 Dongchang Lane, and the other was Gao Yuqing, 35 years old, from Yangzhou. The red pills were purchased from Honorable Girl at the above-mentioned location. Therefore, Zhang Mingqin, the district chief of the district, and Lu Ying, the captain of the detective team, immediately ordered detectives and policemen to rush to the location to search. As a result, the daughter, Lin Ying, was arrested, along with thirteen bags of red pills, six silver dollars, and sixty-eight cents in small silver. Honorable Girl had happened to cross the river from Pudong to Shanghai and had not been arrested. The people and stolen goods were all escorted to the district. He continued to send detectives to wait near Honorable Girl's house until 5 o'clock yesterday morning, when Honorable Girl was seen returning from Pudong. She was arrested by the detectives and escorted to the district. After questioning, she confessed to selling red pill drugs without denial. Because it was related to selling drugs, the district prepared a document and sent the four criminals, the red pill queen Jiang Zhu and her daughter, Zhu Helin, Gao Yuqing, and others, along with the red pills, to the third section of the General Administration for legal action yesterday afternoon.

Japanese Consulate Cracked Down on Japanese Residents Taking Cuts from Gambling, Seven Gamblers Were All Reported, Taking Cuts as Travel Expenses for Returning Home

According to yesterday's Japanese Shanghai Daily News, the head of criminal affairs of the police station of the Japanese Consulate General, after discovering that there were gamblers on Haining Road, Detective Okumura investigated and reported seven gamblers, Niusao Maoji, Tongquan Shanjie, Xigu Tatsu no Jo, Hirano Yoshitaro, Ide Yasuchi, Kotani Iwo, and Matsumoto Nobu, all at once. The motive of the case was that Niusao was burdened by family affairs and wanted to return to his country, but he was troubled by travel expenses and could not set off. On February 14, he visited Matsumoto on Minhang Road and told him, "I am currently in financial difficulties. Is there any way to make money?" Matsumoto replied that he could invite friends to open gambling and take cuts. Niusao was very happy when he heard this idea, so he discussed it with Jianquan on Haining Road. He rented a building at Tongquan's house and persuaded five people, including Ihu, Xigu, Kotani, and Hirano. From 7 p.m. on February 14 to 7 a.m. the next day, they gambled with "four, five, six" dice at Tongquan's house, earning 280 yuan in head money. But Niusao only got 70 yuan. The winners on that day were very big. Xigu lost 1,830 yuan, Ide lost 200 yuan, Hirano won 890 yuan, Kotani won 800 yuan, Tongquan won 600 yuan, and Matsumoto won 300 yuan, but all were not in cash. They used business cards as paper money substitutes to keep accounts. Tongquan and Ihu, because Xigu lost too much, came out to mediate and ordered Xigu to pay 1,000 yuan, saying that 500 yuan would be paid to Kotani and the remaining 500 yuan would be distributed to Hirano and Matsumoto. Tongquan was willing to waive his rights, and the head money would be given to Xigu. Later, except for Matsuki, they gambled again at the original location on the 16th, earning 230 yuan in head money. However, because Xigu's debt was too large, it was difficult to pay it off. He went to Hirano's house on Wusong Road to invite friends to gamble. In total, he gambled three times and got 280 yuan in head money. Unexpectedly, the matter was known to the consulate, so the criminals were completely reported.

Shi Jixiang Was Splashed with Nitric Acid and Died, The Thugs' Whereabouts Are Unknown, Shi Jixiang Was Injured and Died Unjustly

Shi Jixiang from Jiangbei, 45 years old, lived in a bungalow on Changping Road, Xiaoshadu Road, and worked for a living. At about 4 p.m. on the 2nd of this month, while walking near the Labor Hospital with his brother Shi Junyi and others, from south to north, a man suddenly rushed from behind and splashed nitric acid on Shi Jixiang's face and other places without asking any questions. Shi cried out in pain at that time and immediately fainted to the ground, unconscious. The man, seeing that his goal had been achieved, turned around and fled without a trace. Shi was sent to the Labor Hospital by his brother, but the treatment was ineffective. He died of his injuries the day before yesterday. The hospital reported it to the Gordon Road Police Station and ordered detectives to investigate. The body was carried to the Forensic Examination Office on Fielun Road. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, accompanied by forensic doctor Zhang Yan and recorder Wang Zuyi, arrived at the office to examine the body. After questioning Shi Junyi and the deceased's wife Shi Cai, Guo stated that the deceased Shi Jixiang, male, was indeed splashed with nitric acid on his face and died. The body was handed over to his wife Shi Cai to take back for burial after signing a statement.

Chen Chunan Sued by Nephew for Property Invasion, Continued Trial, Must Summon Important Witness Chen Zifang to Court, Therefore, the Trial Is Extended for Two Weeks

Chen Chunan, a wealthy Cantonese merchant living in Shanghai, lives at No. 16 Zhilanfang, Avenue Joffre, in the French Concession. His grandfather had opened Chen Hefeng Tuhang in Shanghai during his lifetime and made a huge fortune. A year or two ago, Chen was sued by his younger brother Chen Xiangnan for inheriting the estate. Fortunately, it was resolved through the mediation of relatives and friends, and the lawsuit was settled. Unexpectedly, last autumn, Chen was suddenly sued by his nephew Chen Jiancheng in the Second Special District Court for encroaching on family property, and he filed a private lawsuit demanding one-quarter of the family property, totaling 2 million yuan. After several months of litigation, the verdict was that Chen Chunan was not guilty. However, Chen Jiancheng declared that he was dissatisfied and hired lawyer Wang Peiyuan and others to file an appeal with the High Branch Court. The court approved the motion and held the first hearing on the afternoon of April 29. In court, the plaintiff presented three reasons for the appeal, but the hearing was adjourned due to the absence of witnesses. The details were recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday was the date for the retrial of this case. Judge Li Changnian presided over the hearing and summoned the plaintiff and defendant Chen Jiancheng Chen Chunan, each accompanied by their defense lawyers. However, Chen Zifang, an important witness in this case and a shareholder of Hefeng Tuhang at the time, was not present, and his address was unknown. However, the court stated that it was necessary to inquire about the situation of the joint venture and opening of Tuhang at that time, so it ordered him to be summoned to court to testify. Therefore, the court ordered the case to be extended for two weeks and ordered the plaintiff to instruct Chen Zifang to attend court in order to proceed with the trial.

Patriotic Youth Zhang Guoxiang Threw a Bomb at Xinghua Restaurant, Originally Intending to Destroy the Facade of Jihua Restaurant, Because There Were Many People Entering and Exiting, He Waited for a Long Time Before Throwing It In, As a Result, Zhang Guoxiang Was Sentenced to Three Months in Prison

Zhang Guoxiang from Sichuan, 22 years old, joined the Volunteer Army to kill thieves for the country during the January 28th Shanghai War. When the war stopped, because the Japanese Kou invaded the Northeast, he rushed to the Northeast alone to cooperate with the Northeast Volunteer Army. When the Tanggu Agreement was concluded, he had no place to use his heroism, and after turning around, he returned to Shanghai. He made a living by shining shoes for others with Jiang Minsheng, a shoe-shining major general. At 8 p.m. the day before yesterday, he took a warning letter and a bomb wrapped in yellow paper to the door of Xinghua Restaurant. When he saw that people entering and leaving the restaurant were constantly coming and going, he was afraid that throwing it would hurt people, so he wandered outside the restaurant for about an hour. Later, because the number of people entering and leaving gradually decreased, he threw the letter and bomb together and ran away. Fortunately, the bomb did not explode, so nothing happened. Zhang ran to Shanxi Road and was finally intercepted by the night watchman No. 551 and the two Chinese constables Nos. 2876 and 1776, and taken to the Zhabei Police Station. After being questioned by the head of the police station, he was immediately detained. At that time, the police station had received a call from Xinghua Restaurant, and immediately sent detective Wang Jiaju to investigate and brought back the letter and bomb. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Special District Court, where Judge Qian Hongye interrogated him. After the police station lawyer Li Zhishan stated the case, he presented Zhang's confession from the police station and requested that the case be handled in accordance with Article 318, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law and Article 200 of the Criminal Law. When asked by the defendant Zhang Guoxiang, he admitted that he threw the bomb. As for the warning letter, he said that it was written by Zhou Kexiang. Zhou was a comrade of the Youth Aid to the Horse Group. He met him at the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Wuchang Road ten days ago. At that time, he went to Zhou's residence at No. 1059 North Sichuan Road. According to Zhou, he was instructed to find a bomb. It happened that I still had one bomb and placed it with Jiang Minsheng, so I took it and gave it to Zhou, originally intending to destroy the facade of his store. When he went last night, he saw that there were many people entering and leaving the store, which was inconvenient to do. He waited until about 1 a.m. and saw that no one was entering or leaving, so he threw the bomb and letter in. But the explosive power of this bomb is extremely weak, and even if it explodes, it can only cause slight injuries. Finally, lawyer Li argued that patriotic actions should have a scope and can be diligently reported through legal procedures. Now, they have suddenly used explosives, which not only damages people's rights and freedoms but also disrupts public order. He asked the court to investigate and handle it. Judge Qian immediately announced the verdict: Zhang Guoxiang was sentenced to three months of imprisonment for possessing explosives for criminal use. The bomb was confiscated.

After the meeting began, Chairman Ni Baiyan delivered an opening speech, saying, "Since the establishment of this association, initiated by six groups including the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, its intention was originally to promote domestic goods. Although we have loudly appealed and announced promotion, we have always been weak in strength and light in words, making it difficult to achieve practical results. I feel even more ashamed.
