Flour Futures Market Shows Increased Activity

Yesterday's flour market saw a steady trend after opening in the morning. Foreign wheat prices had sharply increased, with Chicago up by $1.65 and Canada up by $1.89. This stabilized market sentiment and prices were raised slightly upon opening. However, due to the continuing economic downturn and limited activity in the north, price increases were minimal. In the afternoon, the market remained flat, but speculative activity increased, with some short covering. Prices gradually improved. Factories did not sell much, with major factories trading only 20,000-30,000 bags. Given the current purchasing power, this still felt weak. With the new wheat harvest approaching, the frequent increases in foreign prices were unlikely to have a significant impact. As a result, the price for the current month increased by 2 cents from the previous day, June increased by 2 cents, July increased by 1.5 cents, August increased by 2.75 cents, September increased by 2.5 cents, and October increased by 2.7 cents.

Rice Futures Up 6-7 Cents

Yesterday's rice futures market was calm and normal in the morning. Foreign wheat prices were up by about $1.67-1.89. However, with the market feeling good and rice still available, buyers showed little interest. Prices remained largely unchanged upon opening. In the afternoon, the flour market showed a positive trend and sellers were reluctant to sell at reduced prices. Prices were raised upon opening, and trading was brisk. This trend was driven by foreign wheat prices. The future direction depends on both the weather and prices. As a result, June futures increased by 7 cents, July increased by 6 cents, and August increased by 6 cents. There were no comparisons for other months. The spot rice market saw brisk trading with stable prices. Kai Dangshan wheat was priced at 3 dollars, with the next grade at 2.98 dollars. Xuzhou wheat was priced at 2.95 dollars, with the next grade at 9 cents. Shandong wheat was priced at 3 dollars. Wuhe wheat was priced at 2.88 dollars. Yao Wan wheat was priced at 2.95 dollars, with the next grade at 9 cents. Fuxin purchased an estimated 4,000 bags.

Silk and Tea: Late Spring Silkworm Development in Jiangsu and Zhejiang

(Yuyao) Farmers are raising spring silkworms this year, including Hangzhou, Zhuji, and native breeds. Many in Linxi Township, Tianyuan City, Henghe Town, and other places are hatching foreign breeds. However, the weather has been erratic, with frequent changes. Most native breed silkworms in the second and third sleep stages have been discarded, especially due to the recent hot and cold snaps. Early batches of foreign breeds are already in the major sleep stage, while later batches are still in the third sleep stage. Recently, the temperature has remained low, and farmers are using fire to supplement the temperature for the silkworms. Their appetite is not strong, and development is not going smoothly.

(Fenghua) Farmers are hatching silkworms late this year due to the cold weather and late sprouting of mulberry trees. Some in Puwangmiao, Jiangkou Town, Xixi, Weijiazhuang, and other places are hatching native breeds, but the silkworms are not uniform. Those raising improved breeds are about 5-6 days later than the native breeds. After the leaves sprouted, the cold and rainy weather has been unfavorable for the silkworms. Native breed silkworms in the second and third sleep stages have suffered disease and losses of about 60%. Improved breed silkworms are currently in the major sleep stage, but the weather remains cold and they are unable to wake up.

(Taixian) Many farmers in various villages are hatching their own native breeds. The highest volume is in Dasizhuang, Huai'an, Shuanggou, and other places. The number of silkworms raised in Jiangnian and Majiabu has decreased. After the leaves sprouted, the weather was suddenly cold and hot, with continuous rainy days. Silkworms in the second sleep stage were found to be suffering from yellowing, black vomit, and rotting, with 30-40% dying. Currently, the improved breed silkworms are in the third sleep stage, but the weather remains cold, causing sluggishness and loss of sleep. Their current condition is not good.

(Hushu) In the Hushu area of Hangzhou, farmers are hatching native breeds for economic reasons, accounting for 40-50% of the total. However, the weather has been continuously rainy and cloudy, causing changes in the second and third sleep stages. Improved breeds are developing slowly, with only sluggishness and loss of sleep. In recent days, the weather has been initially hot, followed by a sudden cold snap, with a temperature difference of 30-40 degrees within two days, and thunderstorms. This has caused most of the native breed silkworms to suffer from yellowing, black vomit, and significant mortality. Improved breed silkworms are also slow-moving, eating less, and showing symptoms such as empty heads and white stiff disease.

(Baima) In Baima, Xinfeng, and other places in Jiaxing, many are raising improved breeds. However, the cold weather has caused mulberry trees to sprout late, and silkworms are not hatching uniformly. After waking from sleep, the weather is suddenly cold and hot, with continuous rainy days, which has greatly affected the silkworms' development. Silkworm sleep is delayed. Early batches are just in the third sleep stage, while later batches are only in the second sleep stage and eating well. However, in recent days, the weather has changed dramatically, and most silkworms are stiff and unable to wake up. Some cases of black and rotten silkworms have been found. Mulberry leaves are cheap, costing two dan per yuan. There is no market for the leaves.

The Shen Bao Wireless Radio Weekly

A Novel Detection Circuit

— Ming Xiang

Vacuum tubes are used as detectors, mainly in two ways: plate detection and grid detection. The principle is to make the input high-frequency current unidirectional after detection, so detection can also be said to be the rectification of high-frequency current. Although the detection circuit described in this article is also based on the principle of rectification, the circuit is unique and completely different from the above two methods. Readers may be seeing it for the first time, and this type of circuit has already been adopted in newly released radios, so it should be introduced urgently.

This new detection circuit has three distinctive features: 1. A single detection stage contains two triodes. The first tube makes the input high-frequency current only flow in one direction to complete the detection purpose, so it is called a detector rectifier; the second tube amplifies the weak audio frequency oscillating voltage X after rectification, and feeds it to the audio frequency amplification stage, so it is called a detector amplifier. 2. The signal output is not connected to the plate circuit as in ordinary vacuum tube circuits, but is connected to the ground wire in the grid circuit. 3. No positive voltage is applied to the plate, but it is connected to the cathode and grounded.

Figure One

To illustrate the function of this detection circuit, refer to Figure 1A, which is a simple half-wave rectifier. If S represents the secondary of a high-frequency transformer, it can also be regarded as a half-wave or bipolar detector. One end of the secondary S is connected to the plate, and the other end is connected to the filament via a resistor R. When S receives a high-frequency signal voltage, in the positive half cycle, the plate attracts electrons and a current flows through R. There is no plate current flow in the negative half cycle, so it is completely a half-wave rectification.

Refer again to Figure 1B. The plate and cathode of this triode are connected to the ground wire, so it coincides with end 2 of the filament of Figure 1A. Lead 1 of Figure 1B is also completely the same as lead I of the plate of Figure 1A. The difference is that in this circuit, the grid of the vacuum tube is used as the plate, and the plate is connected to the cathode to reduce the internal resistance of the vacuum tube.

[PＩ>

Figure Two

ＩP]

Figure 2 shows the circuit after the combination of the detector rectifier and the detector amplifier. A closer look at this circuit reveals that it is a resistance-coupled amplifier. The so-called detection amplification stage is nothing more than a preamplifier for the audio frequency stage. Its operating principle is exactly the same as that of a normal amplifier, so it will not be discussed further.

Using this detection method, when the amplitude modulation of an external signal increases, its audio frequency output can also increase in direct proportion, which is its unique advantage and difficult to achieve with other detection methods.

If you want to connect a pickup or microphone in this circuit, it can be connected at the X symbol in Figure 2.

Ultra-Shortwave Oscillation Using Diodes

— Bo Qing

The oscillation of ultra-short waves has always been mainly achieved using triodes, magnetrons, etc. However, recently a simple method of oscillating ultra-short waves using a special structure of diodes has been discovered.

This diode, as the name implies, does not have a grid, and is exactly the same as a magnetron, and does not require a strong magnetic field to be applied from the outside, that is, the simpler it is, the better the oscillation efficiency.

The structure of this diode, B, is slightly different from the past. Its center has a tungsten wire anode with a diameter of 1 hao (1 mm), which is used as an axis, and four cathodes are arranged inside a cylindrical surface with a diameter of 12.5 hao (12.5 mm). The electrons emitted from the cathode cannot be completely absorbed because the anode is extremely thin, and a part of it passes through the side of the anode due to inertia, causing it to be re-attracted by the anode and generate movement. As a result, electrons around the anode oscillate.

The connection situation is shown in the second figure, A and B.

Figure One Figure Two

Are parallel lines spaced 2 centimeters apart, C is a variable capacitor with a maximum capacity of about 10 pico farads, and D is a circular copper plate with a diameter of 30 centimeters, and A and B pass through it.

Therefore, as usual, no plate choke is used, only a choke is inserted on the filament side. The normal output is about 25 milliamps in the belly of a 50-centimeter antenna.

When the plate voltage is at 360 volts, a wavelength of about 1.5 meters can be obtained. Moving the circular plate along AB, or changing the capacitance, can also change the oscillation wavelength within a considerable range. If the D plate is close to the vacuum tube, the wavelength can be shortened, but if it is too close, the oscillation will stop.

According to the connection in the second figure, the influence of the oscillation wavelength is checked by using the change of external constants. As shown in the figure, the length of the parallel line can be freely changed, and the oscillation state of the C capacitor is adjusted to the most appropriate state, and then it is fixed, and only the length of the anode is changed, then the following wavelengths can be obtained:

E Wavelength Anode Voltage

08 cm 94 cm 600 volts

10 cm 102 cm 600 volts

12 cm 106 cm 600 volts

15 cm 118 cm 600 volts

If the same connection is used, and the anode voltage is changed from 560 volts to 540 volts, the wavelength is almost fixed at 140 cm, but the output is considered to change according to the anode voltage. However, limited to a certain anode voltage, or a certain specific wavelength, the maximum output can be obtained. According to the calculation, the period corresponding to the wavelength with the maximum output is approximately equal to three times the time required for the electron to be emitted from the filament to the anode.

New Pocket Radio

— Si Lian

In order to reduce the number of vacuum tubes, Americans are actively researching and have come up with reflex radios. However, they are dissatisfied with the volume and installation, so compound vacuum tubes have now appeared. Ban Jie and the author have recorded it in the previous issue.

The latest pocket radio in the United States uses this. The previous issue’s draft briefly mentioned it. This pocket radio is less than 6 inches high, about 4.5 inches wide, and more than 2 inches thick. It has a beautiful color and weighs about 2 pounds. The tuning dial is placed on top, the speaker is in the middle, and the volume controller and switch are below. The circuit is shown in the figure below.

The vacuum tubes used are two Keller brand. The speaker is a magnetic type with a small diameter.

The dual-gang variable capacitor in the figure is quite special in manufacturing. The remaining capacitors and resistors are extremely small. This machine uses a pentode for high-frequency amplification and a triode for detection. It also uses the reflex method to feed back to the pentode as the first stage of low-frequency amplification and input. The pentode is also used as the second stage of power amplification, so the volume is loud. The 21A7 is a combination tube for rectification and a pentode, so although it is called a two-tube machine, its volume can actually exceed a five-tube machine. This machine can receive local and central radio stations without using a ground wire, and can get good results. Its loudness is really the super-super in two-tube machines.

The Past and Present of Vacuum Tubes

(Continuation 2) Contribution from Philips

(3) The Era of Development: Since then, the development of vacuum tubes has been changing with each passing day. The E415 tube was developed to meet the needs of the times. It is used for special detection and audio frequency amplification, replacing the E409 tube. At the same time, the high-frequency screen grid tube E442 and the power pentode B443 also came out one after another. Up to now, A442, A415, and B443 are still popular among amateur enthusiasts and are considered to be a perfect set of vacuum tubes.

(4) New Trends: Today, AC radios are popular in the world. Most radios use AC power, but in the past, supplying AC power to radios was a difficult problem that could not be solved. If you supply AC power with a frequency of 50 Hz to the radio, it will emit the so-called AC sound, which interferes with the radio. It is quite difficult to eliminate this AC sound. After the emergence of AC vacuum tubes, the previous difficulties have been completely resolved. In AC vacuum tubes, in addition to the filament, there is another cathode dedicated to electron emission, and the filament only serves to heat and has no function of emitting electrons, which is quite different from the old-fashioned tubes. With the advent of AC tubes, almost all of the previous DC radios have been eliminated, transforming into today's era of AC radio. (To be continued)

Shanghai Heming Broadcasting Station is known for promoting getting up early. The radio features lectures and storytelling in the dawn hours, which was initiated by this station. From May 8th, Hong Lou Meng will be broadcast every morning from 7:30 to 8:30, lectured by Mr. Wang Wenbin, the owner of the station, at a frequency of 1440. Please pay attention.

These tubes are produced by a famous American factory, are exceptionally high quality, energy-saving, and durable. If your radio's reception is not clear, it is essential to have one.

Essays

Low Prices and Free Gifts

— Hualing

The fairest trade in the world is naturally "getting two parts of goods for one part of the price." However, in Shanghai, it is not like this, at least it is "getting more than one part of goods for one part of the price." If readers stop and take a look on some busy streets, the most common sight is, of course, the big sales in various large and small shops. And it's like they're taught by the same master, all uniformly pasting white paper on the transparent and sparkling large glass display windows, writing red slogans like "regardless of the cost," "serious sacrifice," "special discount," and "selling cheap at a loss" as if written in the blood of Lao Quan, in various styles, quite interesting.

In addition to such grandstanding, some even specify how cheap they are. Thus, from "10% off," "20% off," all the way to "50% off" and "buy one get one free," and even from "buy one get one free" to "buy one get two free," and from "buy one get two free" to "original price of one dollar, reduced to ninety cents." Obviously, "one part of the price for one part of the goods" is simply not true, "one-tenth of the price for one part of the goods" is a little more like it.

"Original price of one dollar, reduced to ninety cents," pushing the cart against the wall, reducing prices even further becomes a bit ridiculous. Then, there is a change of strategy, playing the game of "free gifts."

Therefore, in addition to "original price of one dollar, reduced to ninety cents," there is also "giving away valuable gifts to reward the patronage." If it is an old Quan's shop with generous hands, it will even generously give away a floor-standing vacuum tube forty-nine-bulb radio, or a ticket for the aviation highway construction prize worth fifty million yuan. This sets a new record for low prices and free gifts in the world. Exactly "how many parts of goods" you can get for "one part of the price," we should ask an experienced and wealthy accountant to calculate.

Such low prices and free gifts are honest to both young and old. Even those European, American, and Japanese merchants who are good at dumping goods would stick their tongues out half a foot, admitting their inferiority.

Teahouse

— Xianxian

One Saturday afternoon, I had nothing to do, and it was drizzling. It seemed inconvenient to stroll on the streets, so I decided to go to a teahouse to "incubate bean sprouts."

This was the first time in my life that I had gone to a teahouse. After I sat down, the waiter brought the tea. Strangely, I found a lot of sesame-like things in the teacup. I quickly called the waiter. It was said that this was what was left from the bird tea drunk in the morning. Hearing this, I understood everything. I realized that bird food could be used as a beverage.

After drinking a mouthful of birdseed tea, Zhang Tiekou, a fortune-teller and friend, suddenly nodded and swayed, asking me how old I was. He stretched out his chicken claw-like hand, calculated the yin and yang for a while, and said that I would become very rich and noble in three years. After he finished, I gave him twelve copper coins and thanked him. Afterwards, I regretted it. I should have waited until I became rich and noble before giving him money.

Then, more than a dozen men in blue short shirts and pants, wearing caps at an angle, came in. I was startled, thinking they were the "eat-speak tea" people as the common saying goes. I hurriedly inquired to the waiter, who said they were here to bid for a rotating credit association. Only then did I put down a stone in my heart.

Several men were busy secretly writing bids and pressing them on the table. After a while, the bidding began. "Three dollars and fifty cents," "three dollars, five jiao, one and a half cents," "three dollars, six jiao, three and a half cents"—everyone made a fuss for a while. For some reason, they disagreed, and a fat man grabbed a long-legged man and started fighting. A small companion pulled out a sharp axe from his side.

Seeing that something was wrong, I didn't even have time to pay for the tea and slipped away in the chaos.

Pawnshop

— Yangzijiang

It's easy to pawn things, but it's hard to redeem them.

Because of the difficulty of redeeming, I have repeatedly vowed never to go to the pawnshop again, but my personal economic circumstances have never allowed me to keep that vow. What can I do? Just pawn it. As Lu Fangweng said, "It is not poverty if there are clothes to pawn." It is truly the end of the road when there is nothing left to pawn!

Although the things I have pawned before are already very worthless.

After being rejected by relatives and friends, I silently came back to check my belongings. Wool sweaters, scarves, and old cotton robes would do, as long as the "shopkeeper" doesn't refuse. I don't care whether it's pawned for much or little. If I pawn it for less, it will be easier to redeem. If I have money, there's no need to pawn anything. It's only when I'm extremely poor that I have a reason to redeem them. Because I have judged that I no longer have the ability to realize that dream of making something new.

I am very experienced in pawning things. While others are arguing and quarreling with the "shopkeeper," I have already taken a pawn ticket and several silver dollars and slipped out. Indeed, the "shopkeeper's" face is ugly, but we have things to pawn for money, and we are really justified. I feel that it is better to go to the pawnshop and see the "shopkeeper's" face than to be sneered at by relatives and friends.

In exploiting the poor, pawnshops are undoubtedly our enemies. But in the sense that they can help in emergencies at any time, pawnshops seem to be our benefactors again.

Tobacco and Paper Shop

— Yun Sun

The term "tobacco and paper shop" seems to be familiar only to people in Shanghai. The reason is that in the metropolis, the sale of cigarettes has become a daily consumable for almost every man and woman. Therefore, tobacco and paper shops have not yet had the qualifications to gain a foothold in other cities. In Shanghai, there are traces of them on every road, even in every alley. Although their business success and organizational size are different, they are all called tobacco and paper shops. There is no clear class distinction. No one looks down on them, saying, "This is a big company, this is a small stall." Their main business is not as reliant on selling cigarettes as they claim. The profit from currency exchange is no less than that from cigarettes. Shanghai is full of vehicles speeding around, and there are crowds of people surging everywhere, struggling for their livelihoods. Therefore, although all industries in Shanghai are in an extreme state of depression, every vehicle is indeed overcrowded with passengers! Everyone hates the bulkiness of copper coins. The exchange of silver coins for small coins, and small coins for copper coins, has become the central business of tobacco and paper shops, and also an important element in the increasing number of tobacco and paper shops. Other items such as kerosene, matches, toilet paper, and stamps are their secondary businesses. Their employees are very poor. They have to get up at six in the morning and usually "close" at ten o'clock at night, working a full sixteen hours. After closing, the small window is still open for business as usual. They finally get to rest at twelve o'clock. It is said that their monthly income is only about ten dollars. They have the same responsibility of supporting their families. They also need to treat customers who buy two cigarettes for three copper coins politely. They are just like the waiters in teahouses, "traveling thousands of miles without leaving their homes." Among them, there are also women who can truly "rely on their own efforts," and they are the "bosses" of husband-and-wife tobacco and paper shops.

The Color, Aroma, and Taste of Soochow

— Yanqiao

Soochow University has been full of spring these days. The spring atmosphere is rich and fragrant, forming a beautiful color, aroma, and taste.

The middle school students' calligraphy and painting research association, which has only two years of history, exhibited its works and held a flower arrangement exhibition a few days ago. Therefore, when we stepped into the forest hall, which resembled an ancient villa, we felt that beauty and fragrance were intertwined into infinite spring light, giving us an incredible pleasure. In the four rooms, we saw calligraphy and paintings on the walls, including landscapes, figures, and flowers, all of which were delightful. Even the stone drum inscriptions and Yan and Liu-style calligraphy were copied with great effort. It is not easy for young people under the age of twenty to achieve such good results. Surrounding us were Chinese flowers and foreign flowers, as if the painter's sketch box had been overturned, with all kinds of colors, making it a feast for the eyes. Deep in the flowers, there were also several cages hanging, filled with sunflowers, hibiscus, and embroidered eyes, constantly singing the self-composed melody of nature, which was really flavorful!

The light in the forest hall was particularly dim. Because it was dim, it was even quieter. A lively university suddenly changed at this time, all entering a state of tranquility and indifference, giving hundreds of students a little adjustment in their lives and environment, which was quite interesting. Not only that, but there was also adjustment on the grassy ground near the river.

Early Display, Late Roll-Up

— Moni

My friend recently opened a southern goods store. Because the price of housing in Shanghai is expensive, he only rented one and a half rooms. The front room is used as a store, and the half room in the back is used to store goods. The place is so small, and there are six employees in total. I said to my friend, "The place is so small, I'm afraid the accommodation problem will be difficult to solve." The friend nodded and said, "Yes! We can only display the bedding early and roll it up late in the store." I listened and was very puzzled. How could they display bedding in the store in the morning and still do business? This sentence is a proverb, and can only be taken as a joke.

But I thought that the four words "early display, late roll-up" were not very clear. After spending half a day thinking, I finally figured it out. Originally, it could only be said to the tailors that they "display early, roll up late," because the tailors sleep on the tables. When they work in the morning, they spread out the clothes. At night, they roll them up, put them away and set up their bedding to sleep. Thinking like this, it felt appropriate. Now, people's stores are small, so they sleep on the floor, and they call it "early display, late roll-up," which is really wonderful.

Opening and Closing Shops

— Weijing

In Shanghai, no matter what it is, there is some mystery to it. Even more so, new shops hold grand openings, and old shops that have been in business for decades hold closing sales, attracting customers from far and wide, packing the stores so densely that the stone counters are crowded within three feet.

I remember that two months ago, a southern goods store opened on a certain road. A week before the opening, the city was already buzzing with rumors that the southern goods store would sell a lot of cheap goods at its opening. Therefore, although the southern goods store was scheduled to open at eight o'clock in the morning, around six-thirty, seventy or eighty people were already waiting at the door. Those squeezed in the innermost layer had smiles on their faces. Even those standing in the outermost layer, watching those who came later squeeze behind them, also showed arrogant smiles.

More and more people gathered, pushing and shoving each other, almost starting a fight. Then, amidst a burst of firecrackers, the southern goods store opened half an hour early. One dollar for a ham, cheap. One dollar for eight pounds of white sugar, probably selling at a loss. Customers, with banknotes and silver dollars clipped in their fingers, desperately sent them to the counter, but the clerks still pretended to owe them too much, yelling. The customers were really swallowing their anger and didn't care.

Also, last year, an old-brand silk shop closed down on a certain road. One day, it suddenly announced a clearance sale. It was unbelievable. It closed the front door and opened a back door. In less than an hour, the upstairs and downstairs were packed with customers, so it simply closed the back door as well. However, customers who kept coming and couldn't get in still lingered at the door for two or three hours without getting tired. Some even went home for dinner and then came back to wait, without any complaints.

It is natural for customers to flock to a shop's opening. Business failure, and a clearance sale, can actually attract customers, which is a bit unbelievable.

Teahouse Sketch: On the Top Floor of the Deyilou Teahouse

— Xiatianwu

Uncle Si Quan, with rolled-up sleeves, holding a birdcage as brilliant as gold thread, climbed up to the third floor of the Deyilou Teahouse.

"Uncle Si! Why haven't you been here for three days in a row? Yesterday, old man Yuan Kun said: Xu's old nanny is playing tricks on you for no reason, isn't she?" Gui Sheng, the waiter, wiped the table with a cloth he took off his shoulder and pulled a chair from the side of the partition.

"Fate! The world is getting more and more wrong. The weather is dry and hot. I have never offended anyone, but I don't know which son of a bitch is spreading rumors about me." Uncle Si Quan put the birdcage on the table as if he were very angry, stuck his hips out backward, and slowly sat down.

"The world is wrong. One has to eat one's fill all day long and chew on empty maggots. There are so many people like that." Mr. Qiu, who was usually the most talkative person here, sat on the other side of the table, creasing his two nasolabial folds into a half-smile as he responded to Uncle Si's words.

Gui Sheng had already brought up the water pipe. "Uncle Si! Have a smoke first, to calm your anger."

Mr. Qiu, impatient, asked first:

"Uncle Si! What's the matter?"

"Alas! It's not my son, I have not even been looking for it. I don't know which ghost said that one day he saw me and the eldest daughter of old Mrs. Xu in the Wing On Company. Old Mrs. Xu said: I often smile at her daughter with infatuation, which is not a good thing. The day before yesterday, she came to me for no reason to stir things up. Do you think this is not annoying?"

"Ah yo! Why do you care so much about such a thing? Qing is Qing, Bai is Bai. If one has money, which place doesn't have young ladies? Such a trivial matter is not worth getting upset about."

"That's not how it is. I'm angry that she's too 'holding' people. She even thought of coming to my face to ask for 0.3 percent. I'm not the kind of person who takes on this dirty title."

"Yes, Uncle Si is originally an upright person. Every day he drinks a cup of tea and plays with his birds. It's intolerable to have people forcibly 'holding' him on to other topics."

Uncle Si Quan seemed to be defending himself and changed the subject.

"Has the head of the firewood guild reached the tenth episode of The Water Margin?"

"It's already passed, already passed. It's been wonderful for three days in a row. Old man Guo is really energetic. It can also be said that he's getting fresher as he gets older. Especially the colors in that section are well done."

"That section? Is it bloody?"

"It's that section. Wang Po received money from Ximen Qing, and she did her best to do the matchmaking. The five-character secret is spoken fluently. The hookup between Ximen Qing and Pan Jinlian is so vivid that everyone who listens is fascinated!"

"Then why didn't you ask me?" Uncle Si Quan seemed very disappointed.

"Uncle Si likes to listen to romantic stories. I was careless and caused you to lose money."

Uncle Si Quan laughed loudly, splashing the water in the cage all over the table.

Let's taste the taste of sports after we finish the quiet enjoyment.

It is fortunate that these three grand events were opened on the first day of the New Life Movement in Suzhou, which gives us an insinuation: "Their new life begins!"

Free Talk

Notes of a Sick Prisoner

— Xiaolong

(V) The Torment of Not Being Allowed to Groan

After the surgery was completed, three nurses of different nationalities—American, Chinese, and Japanese—pushed my hospital bed into the elevator and up to our ward on the fourth floor. Then they moved me to my bed.

The sunlight gradually dimmed. Due to the regulations of the hospital, Lan, who had come with me, had to leave. I was left alone, lying on this unfamiliar bed, among several unfamiliar fellow patients. The air was filled with a sense of desolation in the silence.

The effect of the anesthetic gradually wore off, and the wound in my throat gradually became more painful. I tried my best to endure it. The feeling of pain seems to be more acute when one is lonely. The doctor did not allow me to put my head on the pillow, so the blood constantly flowed into my nasal passages, which made me very uncomfortable. Although breathing was a little more comfortable at this time, because the blood seeped out, I had to spit it out from time to time, which was even more uncomfortable than the shortness of breath.

The sky gradually darkened. The lights in the room also turned on. It was not until after seven o'clock, when the hospital regulations allowed family members to visit patients, that Lan came. Although I could not speak, I felt happy in my heart. The pain in the wound also seemed to be reduced.

Happy times are the shortest. After the clock struck eight, Lan had to leave again. I had to be left here again, spending this painful, long night.

I was tormented by pain all night long. Blood seeped out of the wound and stayed in my throat. You can't help but spit it out. But every time you cough, because you twitch the wound in your throat, you feel great pain. I used all my methods to shift my attention to other thoughts, to forget my pain, but when the pain was severe, it pulled my attention back. My wound was also in my throat, which was no different from a kind of cruel punishment that did not allow groaning, shouting, or making a sound. In this way, I could only silently, persistently, and all night long fight with pain, until dawn was breaking, and just as I was about to fall asleep faintly, a mercury thermometer was inserted into my mouth, and my hand was pulled out of the warm blanket to take my pulse. So I was awakened again by the nurse's examination.

Symptoms of the Times

— Yuanju

In ancient times, there were many famous scholars, especially in the Six Dynasties, who felt that there was only themselves in the world, and no one else. They looked down on the etiquette of the day, broke all the customary ethics, or rolled their eyes at people, thinking that they had deep meaning; or they indulged in wine and willfulness, getting drunk for sixty days—becoming a so-called "celebrity style."

But we, the people who read history, only read the history that has words. Historians are mostly limited to the intellectual class, and only confined to the lives of intellectuals. Therefore, the lives of several other layers of society have not been recorded. Moreover, apart from a few folk legends, the so-called history has been buried by the times.

"Celebrity style" is a kind of "reactionary thought," a manifestation of dissatisfaction with the society of the day, a kind of injustice—but this is limited to a few scholars, most of whom are thinkers who can speak but cannot act, the typical of those who "are not diligent day and night, but say that they travel too much," are "Confucians."

Is social injustice only felt and revealed by a few sensitive Confucians? Apart from a few literati, don't people of other classes feel it?—Yes, they do. The "chivalry" of warriors and the "mysticism" of Buddhism and Taoism can all be counted in this category.

People in the time of the Three Emperors and Five Emperors did not like immortals (there probably were no "Kalachakra dharma assemblies" at that time), and the people were spiritually happier than they are today, the struggle for survival was more barbaric and straightforward, but it should also be more benevolent. By the time society became more complex, and the shackles on humanity tightened, there were people who "abandoned their families to practice Taoism" and "entered the mountains to become thieves." But whether they left the world or entered the world, they could not leave this earth, and the result was still a scourge on society.

The so-called scourge is nothing more than seeking a narrow definition of justice for injustice. Bandits claim to kill corrupt officials, and chivalrous people open their mouths to fight injustice for others. Of course, they also have their own justice and injustice. Unfortunately, they "cannot accomplish their great cause," we only see them bullying the weak and oppressing the few, becoming a veteran dark force. However, whether it is "romance," "chivalry," or "mysticism," the quality of injustice gradually accumulates, all of which are premonitory signs, indicating the future complete destruction and construction of society!

Rouge

— Bai Wei

Miss Duan sat languidly in a soft chair, her eyes emitting an alluring light, her cheeks vividly bright.

"Miss Duan, you haven't been trying your best tonight," Zhi Mu approached Miss Duan and sat beside her.

"No. Mr. Su, I've certainly drunk more than you," she protested. "I already feel a bit dizzy. I don't want to dance; I want to go back to my apartment and rest early."

"That won't do. If you leave, who will enjoy dancing!" Zhi Mu said enthusiastically, "We can't do without you!"

"Really?" This flattery, coming from Mr. Su, whom she had just considered unfortunate, startled her slightly. "In that case, I really should go. Can't you dance with Miss Yu and Miss Wen?"

"If you really want to go back to your apartment to rest, please grant me the honor of escorting you back!" Zhi Mu gazed passionately at Miss Duan.

"Thank you," Miss Duan was clearly pleased. "That's very kind. We'll wait a while and then say goodbye to the hosts together," she replied cheerfully.

Zhi Mu and Miss Duan said goodbye to the hosts and other guests and came outside; it was almost eleven o'clock. Zhi Mu selected a car parked in front of the hotel, opened the door, and helped Miss Duan into the car. Zhi Mu instructed the chauffeur with a few words before getting into the car himself, and the car sped off like lightning.

The two began to chat: from the hostess's new evening gown to the students studying in Paris, and then to the international student dormitories in New York; then back to the French Autumn Salon and their respective departures from Nanjing, Beiping, and Shanghai. Zhi Mu spoke eloquently, and Miss Duan's conversational prowess was overshadowed.

"You were as quiet as a mute at the party, but now you can't stop talking!" She greatly regretted her hasty conclusion about Mr. Su, and said this with a mixture of apology and admiration.

"Now I am alone with a beautiful lady, while earlier I was attending a motley gathering!" Zhi Mu said thoughtfully and solemnly.

Miss Duan gradually grew fond of this Mr. Su, who was knowledgeable and well-traveled, and she was happy to continue the conversation. However, she felt even dizzier, and a sense of nausea arose in her heart. The food and drink seemed to surge up from her throat. She moaned softly, leaned against the corner of the car, pressed her chest, and remained silent for a moment.

"Are you alright?" Zhi Mu asked with concern.

"This car is making me even dizzier. Why haven't we arrived at my apartment yet?" she said intermittently.

"I think we'll be there soon. Perhaps they're repairing the street somewhere, and the car has to take another route," Zhi Mu said, knowing full well that the car had already passed through the center of Paris and was heading towards the Bois de Boulogne.

"I'm afraid I'm going to throw up; what should I do in this car?" she said anxiously.

"Try to hold it in," Zhi Mu, seeing the rows of trees outside the car window receding, knew that the car had entered the Bois de Boulogne and was circling around.

Both fell silent for a moment.

"I really can't stand it anymore! And I feel a bit cold," she moaned and complained again.

"Let me see what street we're on," Zhi Mu reached out and first tightened the belt of her autumn coat, then lifted the car curtain and looked out. "Oh dear, he's taken us to the Bois de Boulogne. How awful! He thinks we're one of those young couples out for a night stroll!"

"The Bois de Boulogne! That will be the death of me!" Miss Duan cried out in despair. Feeling anxious, she almost vomited, and quickly stretched her neck, leaning back on the soft cushion of the car seat.

"It's my fault for not making the street name clear! Since we're here, let's find the nearest hotel where you can rest a bit, or even throw up, and then take another car back to your apartment, okay?"

Miss Duan didn't dare to answer, afraid that the food and drink in her stomach would come up. Zhi Mu pushed open the front glass window and instructed the chauffeur to drive the car to the nearest Grande Cascade hotel.

Arriving at the Grande Cascade hotel, Zhi Mu got out of the car first to reserve a room, then paid the fare and helped Miss Duan out of the car. The electric lights in front of the hotel illuminated her pale face, and her eyes had lost their usual brilliance, her eyebrows tightly furrowed. She lowered her head, not wanting the waiter to see her face. Mechanically leaning on Zhi Mu's arm, she walked into the hotel. The two took the elevator together to room 39 on the third floor.

Entering the room, Zhi Mu gently laid Miss Duan down on the chaise lounge. She lay unconscious, emitting rapid, low moans and heavy breathing.

Zhi Mu pressed the electric bell, and a maid knocked on the door and entered.

"Sir, I await your instructions," the maid said respectfully.

"The lady is drunk. Please prepare a basin, as she may throw up soon. After she vomits, wash her face, take off her clothes, and tuck her into bed. I'll go downstairs for a cup of coffee and then return."

"Yes, sir."

Zhi Mu took the elevator back downstairs.

The next morning, Miss Duan woke up first. She wanted to turn over and look at her newly successful oil painting by her bedside at her apartment. Lying in bed and admiring her masterpiece was her habit in recent weeks - but she was tightly embraced by two strong arms, and couldn't move at all. Only then did she realize that Zhi Mu was soundly sleeping beside her pillow! The events of last night's drunken affair suddenly flooded her memory. She was extremely ashamed, and she didn't bother to resent Zhi Mu, who had toyed with her and was now sleeping soundly. Nor was she in a hurry to break free from his warm embrace; she only buried her face in Zhi Mu's shoulder and sobbed softly.

On the Pinghan Railway Line

— Xu

Although the Pinghan train runs on the great plains, its speed is pitifully slow.

The train is loaded like cargo, with countless people, moving like an ox.

Listen! At the start of the northern section, the train is full of the accents of the Baoding area. People speak with the "er" sound, drawing it out long. In the central section, the simple and sincere voices of the Henan villagers are pleasant to the ear. Further south, each word has multiple syllables.

The train leaves Beiping and soon arrives at the Lugou Bridge. Further ahead, one can see the Yongding River, the great disaster of Hebei Province. During the spring flood season, the river is a vast expanse, the water reaching the embankment next to the railway bridge. In winter, the riverbed is exposed, with raised sand dunes, and water only between the dunes, frozen into silvery-white ice.

Soldiers, bandits, floods, droughts, and locusts travel throughout the land. Everywhere the train passes is desolate. The Pinghan train, with its peeling paint, travels through over a thousand miles of stripped land: everywhere is the same poverty, the same scars.

At each station, vendors wave their goods and shout. Braised chicken recooked multiple times, steamed meat buns with the skin peeling off, sesame cakes as hard as stones, and eggs as small as pigeon eggs are loudly hawked. Buyers must be careful not to receive counterfeit bills or eggs with a moldy taste.

Hunger and cold drive people to deceive!

At Changxindian, one can see the famous domestic repair yard, which reminds one of the Pinghan Railway's past, the demonstration by workers along the entire line against Wu Peifu. Changxindian is a poor place, and the large mound beside the platform has not a single blade of grass.

Arriving at Baoding, one can see the misery of this once-prosperous but now-decrepit city. Baoding station has over a dozen stalls selling braised chicken and pickled vegetables, well-known local products.

Along the way, one can see people pulling plows and elderly couples sighing as they push millstones. When the soldiers leave, the old cattle and donkeys leave their owners.

Dingxian is a famous place; it is on the Pinghan line. At the station, one cannot see the achievements of the Ping Christian Church, but there are vendors loudly selling eyewash.

Many people in Dingzhou suffer from eye diseases, their eyelids red. The Ping Christian Church's sanitation work should show results in this area.

The train moves like an ox. The windows in third class are incomplete, and cold wind blows in at night. First class on the Pinghan train is like second class, second class is like third class, and third class is worse than fourth class on the Beijing-Shanghai line. Passengers think of the Pinghan Railway's own debts, and cannot demand new cars. However, locomotives with "Beining" markings are already running on the Pinghan line.

Crossing the Yellow River, look at the earthen walls of Zhengzhou. Uncomfortable sleep, perhaps in a sense of poverty, passes the forty-four hours and twenty minutes of the long journey.

Insomnia

— Lan Ru

Night, silent night, boundless dark night!

I've started to suffer from insomnia, but it makes me happy. Indeed, insomnia has become something that pleases me. Perhaps some people don't believe me, but I am being completely honest.

Friends whom I forget during the day because of life and work, I remember them all when I suffer from insomnia. When each person's image appears in my mind, I think about many things, such as their lives, their thoughts and actions, their unfortunate experiences, their poverty and future prospects, even problems that they may not have time to think about.

For four or five years, I have often been mocked by my friends, who say I am unfeeling and don't care about them. But heaven knows how much I think of them in sleepless nights, how much I worry about their difficult lives, how much I resent their unfortunate experiences. Therefore, I often thank insomnia, which reminds me of my friends, my beloved parents and siblings, in the silent late night.

But insomnia sometimes does give me pain. For example, during the day I completely forget everything about myself because of busy work: I forget the past misfortunes, I forget the greatest trauma. But when I suffer from insomnia, all the painful memories, the deep scars, flood my mind. They are so terrible, like a knife cutting my liver and intestines, countless arrows shooting my heart, a fierce tiger tearing open my head and chewing my bones, sucking my blood. I feel uncomfortable, I feel great pain, but I can't move, like a paralyzed person who can't even turn over. My chest feels tight, and then I cry!

Every time I have insomnia, I watch the sky grow light.

In all honesty, insomnia has given me many benefits, such as reading, thinking, reviewing the past, and planning for the future. Everything that I don't have time to think about or do during the day can be done at night. I often think that life is too short, and decades pass like a flash. There is too much to do. If everyone could use their nighttime hours as productively as their daytime hours, society would progress faster, and humanity would not lag behind the times like a camel.

It's amazing, but I've been suffering from insomnia for eight years. In Beiping, there was a half-year period when I didn't sleep more than an hour a night. During that half-year, I finished several important books on social science. Although I was very tired during the day, the whip of life lashed heavily on my body, making me forget fatigue, forget pain, and just work for life, and live for work.

Later, life changed, and insomnia got a little better. I could sleep at least three hours a night. But for the past half-month, I have returned to the state I was in Beiping, watching the ceiling turn white.

But I don't curse insomnia; I should be grateful for the benefits it has given me!

The Shanzhuang Ticket (7)

— Tang Xiru

Where to go? Of course he was a rich man, but before tomorrow, he still had to lie on Oyster Shell Street for one more night, although he thought it would be his last.

Tonight was the first night he couldn't sleep because of happiness and joy, which he could only vaguely recall from the night before his wedding at eighteen. But how different it was! From now on, he was a rich man!

Hearing other coolies snoring beside him, he couldn't help but want to laugh out loud. Who would have thought that he had already become a rich man? Ah, farewell, cement sidewalks! Ah, ah, farewell, centipede-legged arcades! Tomorrow night he would sleep on a warm, soft steel-wire bed, he would eat oily food, wear silk, ride in cars.

He was waiting for the rooster to crow, he was waiting for the factory whistle to blow, he was waiting for dawn.

The sky wasn't fully bright yet, but A-Fa had already paced back and forth in front of the entrance to the Xinglong Shanzhuang ticket shop dozens of times.

Five o'clock, six o'clock, the street cleaners had already swept the bottom of the arcades with large bamboo brooms, and villagers carrying vegetables were creaking into the city.

Seven o'clock, eight o'clock, many small shops opened their doors.

Nine o'clock, the big companies opened their doors. More people appeared, and more vehicles.

A-Fa was like a pendulum, pacing back and forth twenty times every hour in front of the door. He had counted the doors of Xinglong hundreds of times. From left to right, there were twenty-five wooden doors. From right to left, there were still twenty-five. Each door panel seemed to be sullenly and elongated facing him.

A kind of ominous premonition was warning him in his chest. But he dared not think, he dared not believe. It would be too terrible.

No, the two extinguished lanterns at the entrance still stood there like door gods. They were trustworthy, which comforted him.

Ten o'clock, tea houses and restaurants were all packed with people, packed with sounds.

Eleven o'clock, twelve o'clock, many students and workers went home for lunch, and the poisonous sun shone directly on the blue pavement, which softened and begged for mercy. But the doors of Xinglong remained closed, and would never open.

Soon many shop assistants ran over and pasted many "flyers" on these twenty-five elongated faces.

He hoped that he was dreaming, that he had a fever. But many voices confirmed that the Xinglong shop owner's escape was real.

He wanted to cry, to curse, to hit people, but he had no strength left in his body. Not a single bit of energy. He just pulled the corners of his mouth down.

He suddenly remembered: he hadn't eaten anything for a day and a night.

Then a wave of unbearable hunger prevented him from straightening his back. (End)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Margin Money

— Hua Gong

One of the characteristics of modern exchange society is probably the so-called buying and selling of gold. Besides its role in displaying luxurious ornaments, gold not only serves as a measure of commodity value, a material for coinage, and a means of payment and storage, but also forms a commodity itself, to be bought and sold, expressing its value in another form of currency. The gold market is the exchange. The buying and selling of gold is probably the simplest form of exchange, because there are only two ways: selling and buying, and all transactions must be settled clearly within a certain period. At the same time, in a modern world where everything is exchanged as a commodity, it aims at profit and completely deviates from the premise of exchange that "anything exchanged as a commodity must have its own use value." Therefore, the buying and selling of gold, which offers little help to life, is also the most typical form of exchange.

At first glance, the most direct and profitable buying and selling of gold is carried out by those like wealthy residents of the foreign concessions, frustrated politicians, managers, compradores, bankers, and factory owners. Ordinary, unrestrained young people, enticed by its "most direct and profitable" nature, also flock to it, calling it "speculation."

In reality, things are not so simple. The fluctuation of gold prices changes with certain global economic conditions and the exchange rates of various countries. As the saying goes, "A single hair can move the whole body." It is even more controlled by large players—mostly banks and money shops, whose transactions often involve thousands of taels, a far cry from the seven or fourteen taels of retail accounts.

Recently, the United States wanted to implement its silver policy, raise silver prices, and actively buy silver. Gold prices fell, benefiting "short sellers"—those who sold a certain amount of taels at a good price earlier, waiting to buy them back at a lower price. Conversely, those who believe prices will rise are called "long sellers." These are all gold industry terms. However, recently the United States suddenly abandoned this policy and sold silver. In a day or two, gold soared by dozens of yuan. The profits earned by short sellers were not enough to cover all the losses. The suicide reported in the May 3rd edition of this newspaper was undoubtedly directly affected, although it involved speculation in day-trade currency exchange.

"Su XX usually...frequented various markets and engaged in gold trading. Unfortunately, his luck was not good, and he suffered repeated losses, amounting to more than 80,000 yuan. As a result, his capital flow was disrupted, and he was unable to make up for the losses. Although he tried every means to raise money, it was all in vain. Desperate, he...suddenly swallowed opium the other day (the 1st)..."

The changes in U.S. monetary policy affected speculators and were not limited to Su XX's suicide. The things that the newspapers cannot and do not announce are much more than those that have already been announced. This is our experience in reading newspapers.

Moreover, there is the undertow of the big players' loosening or tightening of control, and the waves overwhelm the scattered small players. The profit from the buying and selling of gold is only the "spread"—the difference between the buying and selling prices. If there are no waves, how can one make money?

Therefore, when a change comes, the big players can easily sense it and adapt to it. With one move, they can always make money. But the small players who float along, not knowing whether they will live or die, suffer. Many are ruined.

According to those experienced in this field, the buying and selling of gold requires stability, agility, the ability to read the market, and decisiveness. "Scalping"—a gold industry term for quickly buying when you see an opportunity and selling as soon as you make a profit—is less likely to lead to losses.

In short, it is a business for the rich. The rich can make money with one move, while the small-time brokers who "make a living" in the hands of the rich suffer deeply.

The world is just this world!

May Feelings

— Bo Er

Lightning-like time can be seen eroding day by day on the pages of the calendar. May, it's May again. It is our tragic, painful, indignant, roaring, fiery May. From May 1st, May 3rd, May 4th, May 5th, May 7th, May 9th to the May 30th Movement that stirred the entire sleeping Chinese state. Each event has its profound meaning and contains endless great power.

Isn't that so? Scene after scene unfolds before our eyes: The flames of the May 1st labor class struggle threaten the capitalist fortress and are the prelude to the victory of the proletariat. May 3rd is the vanguard of the Japanese imperialist iron hooves trampling our territory—Shandong. May 4th, centered on the intellectual class, unveils the campaign to overthrow traitors and accept the baptism of new culture, shaking the cornerstone of China's old culture that has lasted for thousands of years. May 5th is when Sun Yat-sen took office as the Extraordinary Provisional President, opposing the warlord Yuan Shikai; on the one hand, it is the rise of Chinese democratic politics, and on the other hand, it is the birth of Karl Marx, the founder of scientific socialism. May 7th and May 9th are warlords implementing treasonous acts, and Japanese imperialists implementing grand attempts to seize China. This crisis has agitated the half-dead and half-alive old China. It is the beginning of the Great Revolution and the prelude to the anti-imperialist struggle. The outbreak of the May 30th Incident more clearly exposes the true face of imperialism and is their attempt to directly suppress the Chinese national revolution.

From these days, China has experienced unprecedented great changes. However,

These events seem to be quietly slipping away before our eyes today. People seem to have forgotten. In the past, there were passionate commemorations, support associations, propaganda teams, and revenge-and-save-the-nation groups, and even suicide squads were organized. Now, it is enough to lower the flag to half-mast and suspend entertainment as a memorial. Thus, the Chinese will be ridiculed by foreigners as having "five-minute enthusiasm," "China is forgetful," and "Chinese are only fit to be slaves." Do we really not know how to commemorate? No—we don't need to make formal, foolish movements, enduring hardship and biding our time to save the country. However, as a result, the four northeastern provinces are no longer our territory! The Manchurian dragon flag and the bright red Japanese flag freely fly in the sky, intersecting with each other. What is going on? Rows of jade-green armored vehicles fly out of XX Road and XX Road. Pedestrians stop in surprise, mistakenly thinking that a great war is about to break out. Everyone barely suppressed a burst of cold sweat, taking a breath. It wasn't the start of the war. The armored vehicles drove past, and only then did people feel relieved and restart their numb legs.

Poor old people of China! We stand on Chinese soil, but we dare not speak Chinese, but have to lose color in fear on the road. Why do we have to show such weakness? The country is about to fall, it's hard to be a slave, and embracing a heart full of sorrow and indignation, let us cry out loud:

"Roar, China!"

On Disputes

— Xiang

After reading classmate Bai's article published in the paper on the 5th, I deeply sympathize, but I have some other opinions.

He said that the "Cleanliness Competition in Dormitories" organized by the New Life Movement Promotion Association in the school was met with dissatisfaction by some students, and the main reason was fundamental dissatisfaction with the organization of the student union. Disputes between the so-called elegant self-admirers and the "petty politicians" in the student union are constantly brewing and erupting.

This is indeed a common dark side of the student world, and in a broad sense, it is the inevitable state of politics in every country. Elegant self-admirers, hermits from the forests, are unwilling to compromise, nor are they willing to remain silent. They inevitably often grumble and indirectly criticize, but the result is nothing more than inciting trouble, and the exposure of such disputes often has no good result.

As Mr. Bai said, I know those celebrities in our school well. They usually wipe their noses with their sleeves and use towels as foot cloths, and are used to being unruly and uninhibited. Moreover, they were unwilling to attend the founding meeting of the student union. After the election, they were not on the list, but they were unwilling to give up, so they naturally took revenge on the New Life Movement Promotion Association organized by the student union. The students who practice the New Life Movement are called "running dogs," which shows that they are noble and unwilling to cooperate with "running dogs."

In fact, this kind of dispute is what causes social unrest.
